Paris Hospital Discovers: Wood鳖子 精 Cures Poisoning; Cures 23 Cases of Diphtheria 76

(Paris) Dr. Besso of the Paris National Hospital has been testing the use of wood鼈子 精 to treat various types of poisoning, and even the most severe cases can be cured. Besso noticed that the symptoms of those suffering from diphtheria were quite similar to those who had inhaled large amounts of sleeping pills. He had previously used large amounts of wood鼈子 精 to treat sleeping pill poisoning and was always able to cure it. He then used the same method to treat diphtheria, administering half a ml of wood鼈子 精 per kilogram of body weight per day for 50 days. All 23 people he treated recovered. (Havas, 10th)

Now, the two have proven that the smallpox germ is only this type of Paschen body. From now on, not only can the problem of smallpox prevention be solved, but the problem of treatment can also be solved.

Northwest Inspection Notes 95

— Special Correspondent of this Newspaper, Geng Ya

Overview of Shaanxi's Products

Shaanxi's products: The Guanzhong and Hanzhong areas have fertile land, with agricultural and forestry products being the most abundant. The Shaanbei area has vast land and sparse population, with coal, tung oil, fur, and other products being abundant everywhere. According to the Construction Department's survey in 1933, wheat production was the highest, accounting for over 48% of the total grain production, totaling more than 1.3 million dan. Next were beans, barley, rice, and other miscellaneous grains, also totaling more than 1.3 million dan. The fragrant rice and black rice produced in Nanzheng have a clear fragrance and taste. The cooked rice produced in Wangqu Town, Chang'an, can expand three times its volume when cooked, which can be called a special agricultural product. In the same year, according to the 37 counties surveyed, cotton fields accounted for just over 9% of all cultivated land. According to the Cotton Industry Control Committee of the Economic Commission, the increase in cotton fields in Shaanxi Province last year (1934) was as high as 80% compared to the previous year (1933), with a total harvest of more than 1,004,000 dan of cotton, an increase of 95% compared to the previous year. The land in the Luohe area is even more fertile than that in the Jinghui area. In the future, when the Luohe Canal is completed and tobacco planting is prohibited, the surge in agricultural products, especially cotton, will be even more considerable. However, although Shaanxi Province produces abundant cotton, there is not a single textile factory to utilize the excellent raw materials locally. The hand-woven native cloth is all made using outdated methods, resulting in the undervaluation and export of raw materials, the import and sale of foreign cotton cloth, and the people of the province suffering from economic exploitation through scissors differences. The discussions about establishing a yarn factory in Shaanxi have a history of thirty or forty years. During that time, there were cases of promoters running away with the funds, leading to repeated attempts and failures. A few years ago, several wealthy businessmen planned to raise shares to establish a factory, which was named the Yutai Spinning Mill. It is hoped that it can be realized soon. Also, every time the Hui Canal is constructed in Shaanxi Province, local powerful people invariably compete to buy land at high prices, and the new and old landlords raise rents on the pretext, making it impossible for many small and medium-sized farmers who are tempted by high prices or subjected to economic pressure to become tenant farmers after selling their land. Furthermore, poor small farmers find it difficult to obtain loans directly from banks, and they often obtain loans indirectly, with the interest rate increasing invisibly in the process. This is regrettable.

Shaanxi Province's forest products, such as pear, jujube, peach, apricot, grape, and other vegetable trees, are found in many places. Forests of timber such as pine, cypress, elm, and walnut are abundant in the Qinling and Bashan Mountains. Among them, the lacquer tree is a special product, producing more than 100,000 catties of lacquer annually, worth more than 130,000 yuan. Tung trees produce 160,000 catties of oil, worth 60,000 yuan. The two items are worth about 200,000 yuan in total, which is a major income for the counties in the Hanzhong area. The mushrooms attached to forests and pear orchards in various places are excellent for making delicacies. More than 1.5 million catties are exported annually. Mushrooms grow on decaying wood and are brown-black or yellow-white in color. The planting method involves cutting the wood into sections and placing them horizontally in a shady place without fertilization. Mushrooms will grow within a year, and production lasts for three years. After that, they turn red and yellow. After drying, they smell like sweet osmanthus and are called osmanthus ear, and are priced higher than black ear. If the black ear naturally mutates into white ear, it is also called silver ear, and each catty costs as much as several dozen yuan. However, once silver ear is produced, it will not grow again the following year. Many people raise silkworms in the Hanzhong area of southern Shaanxi. In the past, they were sold to Sichuan and Gansu provinces, reaching 700,000 to 800,000 yuan annually. They are also occasionally raised in Chang'an, Dali, Luochuan, and Yichuan counties.

The first mineral to be mentioned is petroleum. Oil areas are distributed in the counties of Yanchang, Fushi, Zhongbu, Yijun, Jiaxian, and Mizhi. Forty or fifty oil springs have emerged one after another, mostly flowing out of rocks or floating on the surface of the water from the bottom of ditches and rivers, like dewdrops. Residents in the Han and Tang dynasties had already used it to treat diseases and for burning. A factory was established in Yanchang during the late Qing Dynasty and has been in operation for thirty years, but it has not been very effective due to insufficient capital and poor machinery. In recent years, the average monthly oil production has been: 7,200 catties in the 16th year (monthly), 1,016 catties in the 17th year, 29,207 catties in the 18th year, 15,207 catties in the 19th year, 9,385 catties in the 20th year, 7,013 catties in the 21st year, and 6,098 catties in the 22nd year. The production in the 18th and 19th years was relatively abundant, while the oil production in the 21st and 22nd years suddenly decreased. The National Defense Design Committee has recently invested 100,000 yuan to operate it, and it is reported that production has increased again. The future is very promising. This spring, national tomb-sweeping was promoted, and the Xian-Yulin Highway was rushed to Zhongbu County, where the Yellow Emperor's Mausoleum is located. It will soon be open to Yanchang. It is hoped that the mining industry will take advantage of the convenience of transportation to plan the establishment of a large-scale oil factory, purchase new machines, increase production, and refine high-quality products to solve the fuel problem in the Northwest and supply the automotive and other industrial equipment. Coal mines are produced in both northern and southern Shaanxi. The coal produced in Hancheng Tongguan is of the best quality. The Anzishan coal in Hancheng is smokeless coal. If a light railway can be laid or the Yellow River waterway can be improved and transported to Tongguan to connect with the Longhai Railway, there will be no obstacles between east and west. It is not difficult to keep pace with Kai Feng and Zhong Yu. Iron ore is produced in Lantian, Zhen'an, Yao County, Fengcheng, Hancheng, Shi Ji, Ankang, and Liu Ba counties. The iron ore in Tiedonggou, Zhen'an is especially good. The mining area extends along the mountain for about dozens of miles. The ore is in the form of scattered blocks. Locals mine it and set up smelting furnaces, which can produce more than a thousand catties of wrought iron per day. Other minerals such as Lantian jade, Xunyang lead and copper, Nanzheng placer gold, Shangxian asbestos, Qinling jadeite, Lueyang mercury and Jia Yu stone, Fu County and Xionger Mountain silver mines, Xiao Shan jasper crystal, Tongguan magnetic glaze pottery clay, Nanzheng and Ankang fossils are too numerous to mention. Unfortunately, most of them have not been developed.

The northern counties of Shaanxi Province have always produced fur, and the fur-making industry is most prosperous in Dali. Dali was the seat of Tongzhou Prefecture in the past. Sheepskins produced in the northwest provinces are concentrated here, tanned into fur, light and soft, also known as Tongzhou fur. The annual output is about 100,000 pieces, and the business reaches 700,000 to 800,000 yuan. Because sales are not smooth now, it is difficult to compare to the past. Other areas such as Yulin, Fushi, and Dingbian counties produce tiger, leopard, wolf, fox, and other hides, as well as saddles, camel gear, and other items, worth 60,000 to 70,000 yuan annually. The annual output of leather, shoes, belts, saddles, and other products in Chang'an is worth more than 50,000 yuan. Qian County and Weinan counties produce about 20,000 catties of leather rope annually, worth more than 10,000 yuan. The annual output of leather materials in Pucheng and Chunhua is about 60,000 yuan. In addition, the value of woolen fabrics, colored felt, plush carpets, wool pockets, and other woolen textiles produced in Chang'an, Baishui, Fufeng, Hengshan, Sanyuan, Yulin, and Yao counties totals 140,000 to 150,000 yuan. The total value of the above-mentioned fur products, which were previously sold to Tianjin and transported to Guanwai, reached about one million yuan annually. Since the September 18th Incident, sales in Tianjin have been sluggish, so the fur textiles have gradually declined.

The geology and climate of the northern Shaanxi area are quite similar to those of Inner Mongolia. It used to be very suitable for animal husbandry. Now, not only is there nothing to praise, but even the number of livestock used for agriculture in the province is decreasing day by day. According to the survey and statistics of the Construction Department, the number of cattle, horses, and donkeys needed for agricultural use in each county is 365,107. The total number of livestock actually available is only 210,255, and the number of livestock lacking is 154,381. Of the 37 counties surveyed, only two counties have a sufficient number of livestock, and the average number of livestock lacking in each of the remaining 35 counties is as high as more than 4,410. The impact on agricultural work can be easily inferred. The provincial government has now planned to establish one livestock farm and one horse farm each and has requested the Ministry of Industry to send experts to guide them. This matter is extremely important, especially in the northern counties of Shaanxi, where the land is vast and the population is sparse, which has always been difficult to govern. Now that the provincial government is promoting animal husbandry to increase the production of farmers, this is the best way to stabilize society.

Shaanxi Province was the capital of the Zhou and Qin dynasties, but the geographical advantages have not been fully developed. In addition, due to the soldiers, bandits, and droughts from the 15th to the 18th and 19th years of the Republic, the population of the counties has decreased significantly. In the northern Shaanxi area, in the counties north of Fushi, the total population is only 30,000 to 40,000 in areas with hundreds of miles, and few exceed 50,000 to 60,000. Even in the Hanzhong River basin in southern Shaanxi, although the mountains, rivers, customs, and products are no less than those in the Jiangnan region and the products are as rich as those in Sichuan Province (Hanzhong used to belong to Sichuan. Because northern Shaanxi is relatively cold, especially in the Yulin area, which is as hot as burning in summer and as cold as bone in winter, and the wind and sand are wilderness, similar to desert land, Hanzhong was divided to Shaanxi during the provincial division for adjustment), the population density is still lower than that of the southeastern provinces, and there are barren lands waiting to be cultivated and mineral resources waiting to be developed in the counties in southern and northern Shaanxi. According to the survey of the area of ​​official, public, and private wasteland in 15 counties including Pucheng, Heyang, Shang County, Long County, Xie County, Sanyuan, E County, Lantian, Chaoyi, Yang County, Liuba, Fushi, Zhongbu, Luochuan, and Yanchang in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), the total area reached 588,247 mu. There are unknown numbers in other areas that have not been surveyed. Most of the wasteland is in areas where the local people are poor and the people's livelihood is painful, and the natural resources are the most abundant. If the government can sincerely and powerfully immigrate and reclaim the land, provide financial assistance, give them time, and let them use the harvest for themselves, while the government maintains the barren years, not only will the people who have lost their land and jobs respond in unison and rush to it together, but also the practical problems of developing the Northwest and consolidating border defenses will be more than half solved.

Guangdong Province Establishes Overseas Chinese Affairs Council 96

—Director of the Department of Civil Affairs Serves Concurrently as Chairman of the Committee—

Guangzhou Correspondence: In order to handle overseas Chinese affairs, the Provincial Government recently resolved to organize the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee, with the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs serving concurrently as the Chairman of the Committee. Huang Longsheng and nine others were hired as members, and Li Shinan and four others were hired as advisors. Shao Mengzong was appointed as the Director of the Relief Department of the Committee, and Zeng Xiaofeng was appointed as the Director of the General Overseas Chinese Affairs Department. The monthly funding of 2,000 yuan will be allocated from the provincial treasury. The organizational content of the committee is as follows: (Article 1) The Guangdong Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee shall be responsible for all matters related to the emigration, cultivation, and protection of overseas Chinese from this province. The aforementioned matters shall be limited to not conflicting with the powers and functions of the embassies and consulates abroad and the various departments and councils. (Article 2) This council is directly under the provincial government and has one chairman and six to ten members. The Director of the Department of Civil Affairs appointed by the provincial government will serve concurrently as the chairman of the committee. The remaining members will be hired by the chairman of the committee from among those with prestige in the overseas Chinese community. (Article 3) This council shall meet at least once a week. The matters resolved shall be implemented by the chairman of the committee. If the chairman of the committee is unable to attend the meeting due to circumstances, he may designate a member to act on his behalf prior to the meeting. (Article 4) If matters discussed by this council are related to various agencies, the agencies may be requested to send personnel to attend the meeting. (Article 5) This council shall have the following three departments: (1) Secretariat, (2) General Overseas Chinese Affairs Department, (3) Relief Affairs Department. (Article 6) The functions of the Secretariat are as follows: 1. Drafting, translating, receiving, dispatching, and preserving documents; 2. Custody of seals; 3. Accounting and general affairs; 4. Other matters not belonging to other departments. (Article 7) The functions of the General Overseas Chinese Affairs Department are as follows: 1. Investigating the conditions of overseas Chinese; 2. Guiding and supervising overseas emigration; 3. Promoting or prohibiting overseas emigration; 4. Handling disputes involving overseas Chinese; 5. Answering inquiries from overseas Chinese about emigration and providing guidance; 6. Guiding and supervising the organization and conduct of overseas Chinese groups; 7. Guiding and introducing overseas Chinese returning to invest in industries and to travel and visit; 8. Statistics on overseas Chinese entering and exiting the country and on various items; 9. Guiding and handling overseas Chinese education and culture; 10. Guiding overseas Chinese in customs declaration and tax payment and handling matters entrusted by overseas Chinese; 11. Rewarding or subsidizing overseas Chinese; 12. Publicizing government facilities and treatment of overseas Chinese. (Article 8) The functions of the Relief Affairs Department are as follows: 1. Handling relief for unemployed overseas Chinese returning to the country; 2. Designing resettlement for unemployed overseas Chinese returning to the country; 3. Preventing overseas Chinese from being deported back to the country; 4. Preventing overseas Chinese from being deported and illegally recruited for overseas labor; 5. Investigating the treatment of overseas Chinese entering and exiting the country at various checkpoints and protecting overseas Chinese entering and exiting the country and preventing extortion at checkpoints; 6. Handling disputes involving returned overseas Chinese. (Article 9) The Secretariat shall have one secretary, and the General Overseas Chinese Affairs Department and the Relief Affairs Department shall each have one director and a number of staff members, who shall be appointed by the chairman of the committee. (Article 10) This council may appoint overseas Chinese affairs commissioners or inspectors as necessary for official business. (Article 11) This council may appoint consultants, advisors, and counselors to be hired by this council. (Article 12) This council may employ staff as appropriate for writing documents and other matters. (Article 13) The rules of procedure for the meetings of this council and the rules of procedure for the departments shall be determined separately. (Article 14) These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Provincial Government. (May 6th)

Henan Province: Agricultural Revitalization Plan for Hua County, Drafted by the Revitalization Committee Member and the Magistrate of Hua County 97

Kaifeng Correspondence: Henan Provincial Revitalization Committee member Xia Chongjiu and Hua County Magistrate Xie Suian believe that Hua County has suffered severely from the flood. Now that the breach has been closed, they have formulated the Hua County Yellow River Disaster Relief and Agricultural Revitalization Plan to carry out post-disaster work. The plan is as follows: "In August of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), the Yellow River breached at Shitou Village, Changyuan County, Hebei Province. Fortunately, it was closed in February of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), lasting more than half a year, with losses of more than 20 million, and the disaster was unprecedented in history. Just as we were looking forward to recuperating and slowly recovering, in August of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), the breach occurred again, and half of Hua County was still trapped in the raging waves. The Yellow River was surging, with a great tendency to move north and change its course. Although it was closed again in April of this year, the water flow was cut off. Except for the fifth district of the county, where the terrain is slightly lower and the Liuqing River is silted up, and there is still water with a depth of three to two feet, most of the farmland has dried up. However, when it comes to returning to farming, seeds, farming tools, cattle, farmhouses, and drainage all require funds. After the disaster, how can we bear this? If we do not raise a large amount of agricultural revitalization funds to provide relief, I am afraid that the rural areas will eventually go bankrupt and there will be no hope of recovery. Committee member Chongjiu was ordered to come to Hua County and, together with County Magistrate Suian, went to the disaster area to conduct a thorough inspection. Now, based on the number of dried-up farmland mu and the amount of funds needed for various post-disaster relief efforts, we have formulated a plan as follows: (1) Number of dried-up farmland mu: According to the flood in the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), the area is slightly smaller than in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), with an average width of 25 li and a length of 100 li. The disaster area reaches 2,500 square li. About 2,000 square li have dried up. Excluding those that cannot be cultivated due to sand and city construction, village houses, and graves, there are about 1,600 square li of arable farmland, totaling 864,000 mu. (2) Amount of funds needed for various agricultural revitalizations: (A) Seed costs: In addition to land, seeds are the only essential element for farming. According to the price of various types of seeds, an average of 1 jiao 5 fen is required per mu, and 864,000 mu of arable farmland requires a total of 129,600 yuan. (B) Agricultural tool costs: Tools for plowing, sowing, and harvesting are indispensable for farmers. Over the past two years, they have been quickly destroyed by floods, or buried in mud and sand, or eroded by humidity and corrosion, and are useless. They should be purchased as soon as possible to meet urgent needs. According to the average cost of supplementing agricultural tools of 5 yuan per 100 mu, 864,000 mu of farmland requires a total of 43,200 yuan. (C) Cattle costs: According to 864,000 mu of dried-up farmland, about one-third of the farmers with more than 50 mu can find ways to raise money to buy cattle for application. About one-third of those who have strong men can use human power instead of livestock and can barely cultivate and harvest, without the need to plan for them. However, farmers with less than 50 mu and no strong men are unable to buy cattle and cannot use human power instead of livestock. It is impossible to cultivate without lending money to buy cattle. According to two cattle required per 100 mu and a price of 15 yuan per head, the farmers with less than 50 mu and no strong men have about 288,000 mu and require a total of 86,400 yuan for cattle. (D) Farmhouse costs: According to the survey, more than 300 villages have been affected by the disaster this year, with about 30,000 farmers. Most of the original farmhouses have collapsed, and the cost of repairing all of them is too high. Now, one-third of the extremely poor farmers need one farmhouse each, and each farmhouse requires 10 yuan. For 10,000 poor farmers, the total cost of farmhouses is 100,000 yuan. (E) Drainage costs: It is estimated that the existing water area occupies about 500 square li, more than 80% of which is in the fifth district. The sixth and seventh districts also have a little water in the ditches. The reason for the water accumulation is due to the low terrain and the old Liuqing River being silted up by sand. According to the construction plan and drawings of the Liuqing River, a special report was submitted to the provincial revitalization committee last October to request the allocation of funds for construction, totaling 57,228 yuan. If the funds are not easy to raise for a while, some funds can be allocated first to dredge the accumulated water and engage in agricultural work. However, the minimum is 5,000 yuan. The above five post-disaster agricultural revitalizations require a total of 364,200 yuan, all of which are calculated based on the lowest value of important post-disaster matters, and even the extremely poor victims cannot receive the relief. Although the amount is not small, it is because the disaster is too severe. The various funds required by the general majority of ordinary disaster farmers still need to be raised by themselves and are not included."

Shandong Counties Hope for Rain 98

Autumn Planting Has Not Been Sown, Wheat Is Dying from Drought, Flour Prices Are Rising, Making Life Difficult for the Poor

Jinan Correspondence: This year, from spring to summer, there has been little snow and rain, resulting in insufficient growth of wheat. Farmers initially hoped for early rainfall so that even if the wheat harvest was poor, they could still hope for the autumn harvest. However, in recent days, not only has there been no rain, but the climate has been hot and dry, with frequent strong winds. The lush wheat seedlings are wilting, and the weak ones are turning yellow and dry. Since the wheat harvest is not expected, the autumn harvest is almost hopeless. Therefore, the hope for rain is like hoping for the age of plenty. According to the investigation, the recent rainy counties in Shandong Province, except for the Zoushengyi area in southern Shandong, the area from Lixia to Dezhou in northern Shandong, Heze in western Shandong, and Rongcheng in eastern Shandong, have not received a drop of rain. A drought is about to form. Many people from the eastern Shandong area who lived in the Northeast have recently returned to their hometowns with their elderly and children, and the population has increased sharply, and food prices have risen sharply, making people's lives even more difficult. Because Jinan City has convenient transportation, there is no shortage of food, but flour prices continue to rise, which is a serious problem for the general poor. In the past three days, the price of first-class flour has risen from two yuan to three yuan and five fen, second-class flour from two yuan and seven jiao to three yuan, and third-class flour from two yuan and six jiao to two yuan and nine jiao. If it does not rain again in ten days, it will not only aggravate the drought, but the price of food will rise to an unknown degree. (8th)

Songjiang: Sentencing in Suicide Case After False Accusation of Daughter-in-Law's Infidelity 99

Residents Jin Lianfu and Quan Wangcai, residing in Chijia Lane, outside the West Gate, falsely accused Quan Wangcai's wife of infidelity, summoned their son back to Songjiang, and helped him beat and injure her. The woman, unable to clear her name, committed suicide by taking poison. After the elder brother of the deceased, Liu Meichu, filed a complaint with the county court and after repeated investigations, the facts were clear. A public prosecution was filed for the crime of injury and homicide, and lawyer Peng Zhongjun was appointed as the pro bono defense counsel. The criminal court judge Zhang Yihuang officially sentenced the defendants Quan Lianfu and Quan Wangcai, father and son, to two years of imprisonment each for instigating others to commit suicide, as a warning.

Scheduled Dredging of the Erduan Shoal in the City River 100

The city river in this county has been silted up for years. Dredging began this spring, supervised by the First District Office under the county government's order. The entire river was divided into six sections. Except for the first section, from Dongmenkou westward to Guangming Bridge, which has already been dredged and completed, and inspected and accepted by engineer Gu Houxi, dispatched by the Construction Department to Songjiang to open the dam, and the fifth section which is currently being dredged, the second section, from Guangming Bridge to the Xichengmenkou section, has been delayed because the head of the section, Yu Guisun, firmly resigned from his position, expressing his negativity. Yesterday, engineer Gu was dispatched by the Construction Department to Songjiang to urge the progress, and with the unanimous appeal of the local gentry, the acting district head Lu convened a meeting of the Erduan section directors today (11th), and Yang Yunsheng was elected as the director. The dam will be built on the 18th. It is reported that the project in this section requires a wage of one dime and six cents for each cubic foot of soil due to the long distance to the soil dumping site. It was previously contracted by Chen Guozhi, who hired workers to undertake the project. The dam construction project was separately contracted by Jiang A'er. The district office has notified them separately according to the decision, and ordered the police to inform the ships docked in the section to relocate on a specific date to cooperate with the project.

In Xianzi Mountain, a village in Suzhou, the Wang Cailin family of three was murdered and their bodies dumped in Yangcheng Lake last winter. More than fifty lake bandits were discovered near Sunjiagang in Hengshan, Wujiang County, which belongs to Taihu Lake. They were on eight boats, with malicious intentions. They were on four boats, lingering there. The eighth team of the Water Police received the report and immediately rushed to suppress them.

Wuxi: Beating Wife to Death Sentenced to Fourteen Years 103

Zhou Deming, a poor man from Li Lane on Caishinong near Xidou, returned home in a rickshaw at around 2:00 AM on March 2nd of this year. He asked his wife, Tao, to get up and cook him a meal. Tao could not help but resent him and grumbled, which aroused Deming's anger. The two began to quarrel. Deming grabbed a wooden pillow and struck Tao's head, causing her forehead to be broken. She died shortly after. The murderer, Zhou Deming, was apprehended by the deceased's brother and taken to the police station, then transferred to the local branch court. After investigation by the prosecutor's office, a public prosecution was filed. Yesterday, Judge Liu Bingzhen brought Zhou Deming to court and sentenced him to fourteen years of imprisonment. After the sentencing, he was ordered to be detained and await transfer to prison.

Notorious Thief You Guozhen Begs for Death in Court 104

Zhang Yuchang Rice Shop outside Nanmen was robbed of three hundred yuan in cash by notorious thieves You Guozhen, Xu Jinlin, and Wang Xisheng on the evening of the 2nd of this month. At the time, the thieves fled to Zhoupei Bridge, where they were apprehended by the villagers. An old woman, Ren Zhou, was shot and killed by the thieves. The prosecutor's office of the local branch court sent personnel to verify the case. It is reported that You Guozhen, one of the three notorious thieves, is 27 years old and from Tangtou in the northern countryside. He was previously sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment for theft and was released from prison last year after serving seven years. Now he has been arrested again for theft, which is truly unforgivable. On the morning of the 10th, You sent a letter from prison to Wu Zhengrong, the chief of political police, claiming that the robbery of Yang Qinghe Silver Shop on Datieqiao Street was his doing. Chief Wu immediately reported the information to Magistrate Yan, who ordered Yao Fusheng, the director of the trial division, to open a court session for trial at 5:00 PM that afternoon. According to You's confession, he and Chen and others robbed Yang Qinghe of two gold bracelets. Wang and Xu were not involved in the Yang Qinghe case. The gold bracelets were taken to Daihai by Chen for exchange, so they did not get any of the stolen money. He also said that he was suffering greatly in prison and hoped to be executed as soon as possible. After the interrogation, he was ordered to be shackled and returned to prison to await verification.

Telegram Requesting a Change in Silk Industry Control 105

This spring, there was a shortage of silkworm eggs, causing unprecedented panic. Farmers from various villages and villagers from Wucheng Yili and other places came to the city in groups of hundreds and thousands to buy eggs, but there were no eggs to buy. Some traveled dozens of miles back and forth four or five times, but still returned empty-handed, which led to the destruction of the silkworm egg retail outlets and the silkworm model area. The local county chamber of commerce is currently handling spring relief. From time to time, farmers who raise silkworms come to the association to cry about the difficulty of buying eggs. They believe that at a time when rural areas are bankrupt and the region is still raising funds, everyone hopes that the spring silkworms will have a harvest, which may slightly relieve their suffering. However, the silkworms are being abandoned on the ground and cannot be used for production. If a remedy is not sought immediately and left to develop freely, it will not only harm the silk industry, but also have a huge impact on the region. Therefore, the four points of the Construction Department's poor control over silk and the main reasons for the current shortage of silkworm eggs are put forward: (1) Healthy improved silkworm eggs should be produced as much as possible and should not be restricted. (2) The price of the eggs should be purely based on the amount of production and should not be overly restricted. (3) The purchase and sale of eggs should be absolutely free. (4) The dry orchid improvement fee should be exempted, and the funds should still be used by the agricultural farms in various counties to provide silkworm breeding guidance. The above four points were telegraphed to the Construction Department of the provincial government yesterday, requesting that the original control measures be cancelled as soon as possible, in order to save the silk industry and benefit the region. Otherwise, the rural economy will collapse faster, and the industrial and commercial sectors will be severely hit.

The Houmei Business Group branch in the Seventh District was reorganized in October last year, with Xu Jinying as the team leader, Xu Shijun as the chairman of the board of directors, and Meng Jiafu and others as directors. Huaiyin: Major Fire in Xiba Town 110

Xiba Town in the Second District of this county has about 3,000 households, mostly supervisors. Most of their residences are thatched houses, and fires occur from time to time. On the afternoon of the 7th, a family member of Sun Youfa in Yangjia Wharf was found. The men went to work on the Huai River entering the sea project, and the women went out to gamble, causing their six-year-old child to play with fire at home, which ignited the straw pile and spread to the houses. At that time, the southwest wind was strong, and the fire spread from the south of the street to the north of the street. All the houses close to the neighbors were burned to the ground. Subsequently, the fire brigades went to rescue, and fortunately it was daytime, so they were able to extinguish the fire. However, more than ten houses on the south and north sides of the street were burned, and more than seventy thatched houses were destroyed. More than ten households were affected, all of whom were poor and helpless. After the disaster, all means of livelihood were cut off, and the situation was extremely miserable.

Pinghu: Steamboat Drowns Swimmer 111

A man surnamed Lou from Zhapu Rope Industry, 22 years old, was skilled in swimming. He came to the city this year and worked as a partner in the machine rope shop next to the Yuexian Hotel outside Dongmen. Yesterday the weather suddenly became hot, rising to 83 degrees Fahrenheit in the afternoon. Lou went to Donghu to swim and bathe. A Hai Zi Ban steamboat arrived at the port, and the wake of the boat struck him. Lou was unable to support himself and sank. The owner of the shop, surnamed Ma, found out and had people fish him out, but he had already died. His body is now displayed on a bamboo raft, waiting for his sister, who is married in Shanghai, to come to Pinghu to collect the body. When the boat's wake struck him, Lou shouted for help, but the people on the shore thought he was playing and ignored him, resulting in this disaster.

Local News

Rong Zongjing Hosted the Press Yesterday to Visit Shenxin Fuxin Factories; Large Scale, Perfect Equipment, Strict Management 112

Rong Reported the Establishment of Industrial Enterprises and Hoped the Financial Community Would Consider the Textile Industry and Provide Assistance

Rong Zongjing, a magnate in China's cotton yarn and flour industry, invited the press to visit Shenxin No. 9 Factory and Fuxin Flour Factories Nos. 2 and 8 at 2 PM yesterday, in order to ensure that all sectors of society truly understood the business he had dedicated his life to. More than 50 reporters from various newspapers attended the visit, led by Rong himself and factory staff. They were treated attentively and reported on the latest situation of each factory.

Reception and Visit

Yesterday, more than 50 reporters from various newspapers were invited. They gathered at the Shenxin General Office at 421 Jiangxi Road at 1 PM, and at 1:30 PM, they took two large buses specially arranged by the Shanghai Moving Company to Shenxin No. 9 Weaving Factory at 140 Macau Road. Rong Zongjing, Tian Xialin, Director of the Cotton Department, Xue Guanqun, Director of General Affairs, Rong Shouxuan, Secretary Sun Beixuan, and others warmly welcomed them. They entered the factory's large reception room, rested briefly, and at 2:15 PM, Rong led Factory Director Wu Kunsheng, Deputy Factory Director Chen Pinsan, and Engineer Wu Shihuai to visit the equipment of Shenxin No. 9 Factory and Fuxin Nos. 2 and 8 Factories. The visit lasted for two hours before it was completed. They then returned to the original place for tea and refreshments. Rong delivered a welcome speech and reported on the situation of Shenxin factories. At 5:30 PM, they took the factory's special bus back to the General Office on Jiangxi Road and dispersed. The visit went as follows:

Equipment of No. 9 Factory

Shenxin No. 9 Factory evolved from the original Sanshin New Yarn Factory. The base is large, the factory building is magnificent, and it is located on the Wusong River, making waterway transportation very convenient. The factory's equipment and the thoroughness of its management are often the best among Shenxin factories. For example, the adjustment of light and air in the factory is in a superior position among the yarn factories in China. The reporters from various newspapers, led by Rong and others, first visited the employee dormitory, employee hospital, employee club, consumer cooperative, barber shop, and school for workers' children and other public welfare and health facilities, and then visited raw materials, roving, yarn, reeling, sizing, warp, weaving, inspection, polishing, singeing, dyeing, printing, and packaging departments. According to the staff who led the visit, the factory originally had 1,000 looms, but they were repeatedly eliminated due to the aging of the machine bodies. There are currently 515 looms. Many of the machines in the yarn spinning workshop were made by Howard & Bullough Acerington, England in 1932, which shows Rong's efforts to rejuvenate himself in the global recession and develop his career. It is heard that the factory also has thousands of the latest silent spindles. The factory covers an area of ​​50 acres and has three newly built three-story concrete and steel frame yarn and cloth factory buildings, which are divided into: (1) Machine parts: 80,556 fine yarn spindles, 15,060 thread spindles, 515 looms, 3 printing machines, 1 singeing machine, 2 dyeing machines, (2) Yarn and cloth products: 10-count, 16-count, 20-count, 32-count, 41-count, 60-count, singeing thread and various twisted three-strand wool, dyed embroidery thread, plain cloth, twill cloth, flannel, poplin, thread drill, thread serge, and flour sacks. (3) Yarn and cloth production: 150 pieces of 20-count yarn are pulled every day, 1,400 pieces of 10-pound cloth are produced every day, 10 pieces of 42-count thread are produced every day, 5 pieces of 60-count thread are produced every day, and 40,000 flour sacks are produced every day. (4) Yarn and cloth cost: 345 catties of cotton are used for each piece of 20-count yarn, 40 yuan is spent for each piece of 20-count yarn, and 1 yuan and 1 jiao and 2 fen are spent for each 10-pound cloth. (5) Number of male and female workers: 3,810 day and night workers in the yarn factory, 250 day and night workers in the thread factory, 950 day and night workers in the cloth factory, and 50 in dyeing and singeing, for a total of 5,060 workers in the yarn and cloth factory. (6) Workers' wages: The maximum wage for male workers is 1 yuan and 4 jiao, the minimum wage for male workers is 3 jiao and 2 fen, the maximum wage for female workers is 1 yuan and 1 jiao, the minimum wage for female workers is 3 jiao, the average wage for male and female workers is 4 jiao and 5 fen, and the total monthly wage is 53,000 yuan. (7) Employee dormitory: Special zone staff family dormitory, bedroom for female worker training workers in Zone 1, a total of 50 rooms, currently housing 524 people, Zone 2 single female worker dormitory, a total of 120 buildings, currently housing 611 people, Zone 3 worker family dormitory, a total of 33 buildings, currently housing 594 people, Zone 4 single male worker dormitory, 33 rooms, currently housing 401 people, the factory houses a total of 2,130 workers, Zones 1 and 4 are two-story complete concrete and steel frame buildings, cold and hot tap water, iron beds, canteens, sanitary toilets, bathhouses, washrooms, reading rooms, and classrooms are fully equipped. All female workers in Zones 1, 2, and 3 must take a bath in the Zone 1 bathroom once a day, and male workers in Zones 3 and 4 must take a bath in the Zone 4 bathroom once a day. Male and female workers are forced to read for one hour every day. (8) Public welfare and health matters: The employee hospital is a five-story western-style building with one medical director, one female director of obstetrics, two female nurses, and one Chinese medicine doctor. All employees of the factory can receive free diagnosis and treatment. (9) Employee club: Reading room, library, billiards room, basketball team, tennis team, football team, billiards team, Peking opera troupe, drama troupe, music class, and martial arts group. All employees can join and have fun during the scheduled opening hours. (10) Consumer cooperative: The factory's yarn, cloth, and all household items are available at low prices. All workers in the factory can enjoy this right. (11) Barber shop: The barbers are provided with food and accommodation by the factory, and all male and female workers can get a haircut at a low price. (12) Educational facilities: School for workers' children, night school for male workers, morning school for male workers, night school for female workers, and agricultural school for female workers. All factory staff are volunteer teachers. All male and female workers in the factory, regardless of age, are forced to attend school. Those with better grades and diligent work on weekdays will be promoted to staff members or instructors as a reward. (13) Public welfare and health compensation expenses: 500 yuan per month for the hospital, 100 yuan per month for worker dormitory consumption, 50 yuan per month for scholarships, 50 yuan per month for the club, 50 yuan per month for the consumer cooperative, 30 yuan per month for the barber shop, and about 2,000 yuan per year for compensation for deceased workers.

Fuxin No. 2 Factory

After visiting the factory, they passed through Moxianshan Road and entered the Fuxin No. 2 Flour Factory. This factory has a 1,800-horsepower engine to drive various machines in the entire eight-story factory building. All employees are male workers, and the number is very small, because only three to five people are needed to manage each wide floor of machinery. Rong did not report on Fuxin, so we could not know the specific production and sales situation.

Rong's Report

At about 4 o'clock, the reporters returned to the reception room of Shenxin No. 9 Factory for tea and refreshments. In addition to distributing welcome speeches, Rong also made a brief report, saying: "I came to Shanghai at the age of 20. Seeing the situation, I knew that developing the cotton yarn, cloth, and flour business for people's clothing and food was the most important plan. Therefore, I founded yarn factories and flour factories. In 1918, when the European War broke out, I took the opportunity to sell flour overseas, totaling about 800,000 tons, and after making a profit, I expanded and developed, setting up factories in Hankou, Jinan, and other places, which were watched by foreign yarn factories and flour factories. However, in recent years, due to the global recession, my business has inevitably been affected. Although I am still working hard to break through this difficulty, I also hope that all sectors of society can share this heart and jointly seek the development of China's industry. Then I will be very fortunate."

Rong's Speech

Rong Zongjing delivered a welcome speech at the reception for the press yesterday, saying: "I am very honored that you have come today. I rarely have the opportunity to meet with you, so I will briefly describe the establishment of industrial enterprises, the current difficulties, and future hopes. I hope you will listen carefully and teach me. Forty years ago, I saw that imported goods were becoming more and more popular and that profits were flowing out. Therefore, I had the idea of ​​establishing industrial enterprises. At that time, there were not many commercial enterprises in our country, and the number of foreign flour and foreign yarn sold in our country was already large. Therefore, I invited comrades and planned to establish flour factories and textile factories. Up to now, it has been more than 30 years. We have established 12 flour factories and 9 textile factories. The establishment of textile factories is even more difficult than flour factories. In 1915, Shenxin No. 1 Factory was established on Baihe South Road in Shanghai (now divided into eight factories). In 1919, No. 2 Factory was established on Yichang Road in Shanghai. At the same time, No. 2 Factory was established outside the Five-Hole Bridge in Ximen, Wuxi. In 1920, No. 4 Factory was established in Zongguan, Qiaokou, Hankou. In 1925, Deda Yarn Factory in Yangshupu was purchased as the fifth factory, and the sixth factory was rented outside Nandou in Changzhou. Later, the textile industry was affected by the global recession and plummeted. For example, Housheng on Lan Road in Yangshupu, Dongfang on Yangshupu Road, and Erxin were successively liquidated. We resolutely came out to maintain the unemployed workers and reorganized them into Shenxin Nos. 6, 7, and 9 factories. The place where you are invited today is Shenxin No. 9 Factory, which evolved from Sanshin Yarn Factory. Looking back over the past 30 years, I dare not say that I have benefited society and the country, but I have solved the problem of people's clothing and food. I have gone through all kinds of hardships, but I have never dared to slacken in this ambition. Now the textile factory has 590,000 yarn spindles and more than 5,000 looms, and can produce 1,300 pieces of yarn and more than 10,000 pieces of cloth every day and night. Knowledgeable people think that it is difficult to start a business, but they do not know that it is even more difficult to maintain it. Foreign merchants set up factories in our country, implement their economic aggression, and the dumping policy is the only fatal injury to the textile industry. The operating capital and interest rates of foreign factories are very low. The cost of finished goods is light, and sales are easy. There are no capitalists in our country. The establishment of industrial enterprises depends on the financial community. In recent years, cotton has been expensive and yarn has been cheap, and there is no way out for business. The unified tax still has to be paid, and the interest rate cannot be reduced. Only I can say and bear this kind of pain. Last year, there was a problem in our company's financial turnover, and business was difficult. I dared not complain and still took on the burden myself, and I also regarded running a business as my second life. If I do not fight to the end, more than 30 years of hard work will be in vain. Fortunately, the government has a clear understanding and has long had the determination to provide assistance. Although the seventh factory has gone through twists and turns, it has fortunately not stopped work. Although the second and fifth factories have stopped work, they are still trying to resume operations. In the future, the financial community will be able to take into account the endangered textile industry and provide assistance within the possible scope. The bandit suppression work is completed, yarn sales are smooth, and the market will turn for the better, which is also expected. As for raw materials, various provinces and cities have implemented the promotion of mechanical cotton, and the cooperative is the backing for the revitalization of rural areas. In a few years, it will not be difficult to stop the leakage of cotton imports from outside the country. You are engaged in journalism and are the teachers of the people. I am willing to share the responsibility with you for manufacturing and publicizing domestic goods. Shenxin factories are scattered in various places, making it difficult to guide you to visit them one by one, but in terms of work and management, visiting one place in the ninth factory can cover the rest. I also hope to criticize it and improve it further. I am looking forward to it."

Overview of Each Factory

Rong continued to report on the overview of Shenxin factories (comparison between 1922 and 1934): (1) Regarding the machinery of Shenxin factories, in 1922, there were 517,624 yarn spindles, and in 1934, there were 552,716 yarn spindles, an increase of 35,092; in 1922, there were 40,040 thread spindles, and in 1934, there were 49,748 thread spindles, an increase of 9,708; in 1922, there were 2,902 looms, and in 1934, there were 4,872 looms, an increase of 970. (2) Regarding the cotton consumption and output of Shenxin factories, in 1922, 2,080,417 dan of cotton were consumed, and in 1934, 1,052,597 dan were consumed, a decrease of 27,820 dan; in 1922, 306,465 pieces of yarn were spun, and in 1934, 304,567 pieces of yarn were spun, a decrease of 1,898 pieces; in 1922, 1,798,886 pieces of cotton cloth were woven, and in 1934, 2,346,448 pieces of cotton cloth were woven, a decrease of 452,038 pieces; in 1922, 226,646 blankets were woven, and in 1934, 96,986 blankets were woven, a decrease of 129,660 pieces. (3) Regarding the cost of Shenxin factories, in 1922, the raw material foreign cost was 51,417,284.85 yuan, pulling each dan at 47.59 yuan; in 1934, it was 47,338,977.21 yuan, pulling each dan at 44.97 yuan, a decrease of 4,078,307.64 yuan; in 1922, the labor cost was 5,878,440.09 yuan, and in 1934, it was 4,145,686.21 yuan, a decrease of 1,728,754.71 yuan; in 1922, the material cost was 3,002,018.35 yuan, and in 1934, it was 2,188,823.39 yuan, a decrease of 812,194.96 yuan; in 1922, the electricity cost was 2,625,919.33 yuan, and in 1934, it was 2,147,546.99 yuan, a decrease of 478,372.34 yuan. The results can be seen at a glance. According to the reduction of internal expenses of each factory, there are amazing figures, among which labor is the largest, followed by materials, but the interest item not only does not decrease, but also increases by more than 400,000 yuan. This low-interest loan is the urgent need for today's relief of industry and commerce. I hope that the financial community can sympathize with the appeal of various industries and provide assistance.

Shenxin's Position

Shenxin's position in China's textile industry, the total number of yarn spindles, thread spindles, and looms in the country is as follows: (1) Yarn spindles: 4,621,357, of which 2,627,473 are Chinese merchants, 1,790,148 are Japanese merchants, and 182,196 are British merchants. Shenxin accounts for 12% of the total number of yarn spindles in the country and 11% of the total number of yarn spindles in the country's Chinese merchants. (2) Thread spindles: 408,560, of which 135,860 are Chinese merchants and 272,700 are Japanese merchants. Shenxin accounts for 10% of the total number and 37% of the total number of Chinese merchants. (3) Looms: 39,565, of which 19,081 are Chinese merchants and 17,592 are Japanese merchants. Shenxin accounts for 12% of the total number and 26% of the total number of Chinese merchants.

Comparison of Expenses

The expenses of each factory, including salaries, insurance, interest, unified tax, and other items, totaled 21,543,924.37 yuan in 1922 and 17,966,691.43 yuan in 1934, a decrease of 3,577,232.94 yuan. Looking at the comparison of the above items, a general overview of the general situation of the company's factories in the past three years can be obtained. However, the following points must be further explained to all sectors of society: (1) In recent years, China's industrial and commercial industries have been frequently affected by the dumping of foreign goods, the decline of rural areas, and the decline of the social economy, and there is a precarious situation. The textile industry has been the most affected. However, the company still adheres to the original intention of promoting domestic goods and engaging in mass production. In this difficult period, it has still worked hard to add 15,090 yarn spindles, 9,708 thread spindles, and 970 looms in the past two years. (2) The company believes that improving the output is the only important plan for the future development of the industry, and reducing expenses to reduce costs is also an urgent task. Looking at the above comparison of items, the company has vigorously implemented a tightening policy without leaving any effort.

The Jiangsu Provincial Government Borrows Money from Shanghai Banking Syndicate 114

Using Business Tax as Collateral; the Contract is Said to Have Been Signed

According to the Dagong News Agency, Zhao Dihua, the director of the Jiangsu Provincial Finance Department, said that from April to August every year, the time is between the old and new crops, tax revenue is short, and the provincial government's expenses are always insufficient. In April of last year, the department used the province's business tax to borrow 2 million yuan from the Shanghai banking community, which was repaid in monthly installments. It has been fully repaid by February of this year. According to news from the Shanghai financial community yesterday, the Jiangsu Provincial Finance Department is now borrowing 1.5 million yuan from the Shanghai, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Jiangsu four banks with the province's business tax as collateral, which will be repaid in eight months. The interest rate remains the same, and the contract has been signed. However, the department has not yet allocated it, preparing to use a part of it as political expenses and a part to organize small loans to help the poor people in the province.

Page 12

The Ministry of Communications Orders the Shipping Bureau to Revoke Protection for Foreign Ships Transporting Drugs; Based on the League of Nations Resolution, Three Measures for Prohibition Are Jointly Formulated 118

The Ministry of Communications ordered the Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau yesterday, saying: "It is hereby notified by order of the Executive Yuan that when the 18th Advisory Committee on Opium of the League of Nations previously held a meeting, our country's representative Hu Shize stated that at a time when our country is strictly prohibiting opium, a small number of foreigners and foreign ships are found to be privately selling and manufacturing narcotic drugs in China in order to make huge profits and destroy our country's prohibition policy. In order to prevent this, a proposal was submitted to the committee, which was passed and recommended that the Council of the League of Nations transfer it to the governments of all countries with extraterritorial jurisdiction in China for the adoption of three prohibition measures, namely: (1) Those people of each country who participate in the private manufacture or private transportation of narcotic drugs in China shall be severely punished; (2) The ships of each country sailing in China, if found to be used for the private sale of opium, should immediately have their protection revoked. This case has now been formally notified to our country by the Council of the League of Nations, and it shall be implemented immediately. In addition to the Executive Yuan notifying the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to immediately inform the embassies of all related countries in China and the ministries, commissions, and provincial and municipal governments, and taking the third item as within the scope of the Ministry of Communications' authority, it is specially ordered to implement it in accordance with the ministry. Now, a copy of the original measures is specially copied and sent to the bureau and all its subordinate offices. If foreign ships are found to be violating the opium prohibition and privately transporting opium in the future, they shall all be handled in accordance with this proposal, and the handling situation shall be reported at any time. This order has been followed by the shipping bureau and has been forwarded to all its subordinate offices to comply with it."

After Water Fee Reduction - Users' April Water Bills to be Deducted in May Bills 128

The Shanghai Waterworks Company is to charge 75% of the original water price from April onwards. However, as the water bills for that month have already been collected, the deduction will be made in the May water bills. The company's notice is recorded below: "To whom it may concern, regarding the notice of this company published in various newspapers on May 3, 1935, we hereby reiterate it for clarity. The text is as follows: 'Shanghai Waterworks Company Notice: Regarding the reduction of water fees for users within the contract scope of the工部局 and the Shanghai Waterworks Company, the water bills for users within the contract scope of the 工部局 and our company were already calculated at 80% of the original price last year. From April 1, 1935, the reduction percentage will be increased for bills issued based on water meter readings, i.e., the monthly bills will be calculated at 75% of the original price. For any errors in the numbers on the bills already issued for April 1935, corrections can be made in the May 1925 [sic] bills.' The numbers provided in the attached May bill are the net amounts after verification, which are calculated at 75% of the original price. The other number listed below, followed by 'CR', is the amount to be refunded due to the increased discount percentage in your April bill. The number listed at the end is the net amount you owe our company. All subsequent bills will be issued with net amounts. We hereby inform you. Please check and pay the bills on time.敬具"

Ministry of Finance Reissues Directive - Delivery Receipts Exempt from Stamp Tax - However, Delivery Notices Should be Taxed 131

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Coal Industry Association enclosing samples of delivery receipts and delivery notices from the Da China Coal Ball Company, requesting instructions on stamp tax. The original samples were forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for interpretation. The Ministry of Finance issued a directive on May 8, Tax No. 5383, stating that the facsimile telegram and attachments were all understood. Upon investigation, the sample of the delivery receipt from the Da China Coal Ball Company is equivalent to a delivery invoice, which should be taxed according to regulations. The second copy is the receipt, and the third copy is the stub, both of which can be exempted from taxation according to regulations. The delivery notice contains the phrase "Coal balls of so many tons are paid with this voucher," which is no different in nature from the current regulations for vouchers for various goods issued by shops. The 印花 tax should still be affixed according to regulations. In addition to the fact that the receipt should not be taxed, the tax authority has ordered the Shanghai Concession Tobacco Inspection Office to be notified. This is hereby notified.

The Jin-Engraved Surangama Sutra is Published 134

The Shanghai Engraved Song Edition Tripitaka Society previously entrusted Fan Cheng Monk to seek ancient scriptures in Shanxi, and discovered a scroll-style Jin Tripitaka in Zhaocheng, which is an orphan copy unseen in the world. It is a pity that it is incomplete due to the age. In particular, those who commonly chant, such as the Avatamsaka Sutra, the Lotus Sutra, and the Amitabha Sutra, lack the most. Fortunately, the entire Surangama Sutra is complete and flawless, and it was immediately borrowed to Shanghai to be engraved in the original style. Each volume has one side of the original version, with twenty-three horizontal lines and fourteen characters vertical, and is printed with variable-layer fine paper. The inner core is rolled with a round wooden axis, and the outside is tied with bamboo, without losing any authenticity. The content of the scripture is originally刻 accurate, and when compared with the current moment, the differences, additions and subtractions are as many as hundreds of words. The Nanjing National Academy of Chinese Studies Library, the Zhenjiang Shao Zong Library, and the Suzhou Honghua Society all believe that the display and worship are extremely solemn, and the study and recitation are also free from errors. Special introduction, each set of ten volumes, stored in two exquisitely crafted cloth cases, is priced at six yuan, plus postage of 6 corners and 2 points for nonlocal areas. If there are large donations and the purchase of more than ten sets, there are still preferential treatment. The Shanghai Engraved Song Edition Tripitaka Society is at 714 Weihai Road, and its circulation is quite extensive.

Chaozhou Association: Promoting Thrift Among Fellow Villagers - Thrift Society to be Established Today 141

The Jinzhou Sojourners' Association in Shanghai, in light of the decline in social customs, the extravagance of habits, and the weakening of the national spirit, which are deteriorating daily and greatly impacting the future of the entire nation, has decided to address this downward trend by first promoting thrift among fellow villagers. They are organizing a Thrift Society, establishing Thrift Covenants, widely recruiting fellow villagers as members, and jointly promoting these covenants. The current immediate goal is to improve outdated customs, setting certain standards for weddings, funerals, celebrations, social events, and social interactions, emphasizing simplicity, strongly rejecting hypocrisy, abolishing all outdated regulations, limiting banquets and congratulatory gifts, conserving resources, and avoiding wastefulness. The more than fifty covenants are practical, easy to implement, and promote gradual and sustained progress, aiming to restore China's inherent thrift. After months of preparation, everything is now in order, and the establishment ceremony will be held today (the 12th) at 3 PM at the association's headquarters in Shengping Lane, Gongguan Road, in the French Concession. In addition to the ceremony, members will recite oaths of commitment. It is reported that all Chaozhou compatriots living abroad are welcome to join the society as members, without any fees. The origins of the organization are outlined below:

Since ancient times, our country has been founded on etiquette and moral principles. Social occasions such as weddings, funerals, and celebrations all embody extremely pure and profound meanings. However, in recent times, social customs have deteriorated, habits have become corrupt, and there is a competition for extravagance. Complex and elaborate formalities are merely wasteful and contribute nothing practical, gradually losing their original meaning. The unnecessary waste of time and money is appalling, and the impact on the expression of the entire national spirit is extremely significant. With the eastward advance of Western influence and China subjected to various forms of aggression and oppression by imperialists, etiquette and moral principles have been abandoned, and culture has fallen behind. Instead of adopting the spirit of self-improvement, we have been harmed by the world's material civilization, leading to extravagance, indulgence, and extreme desires, resulting in poverty, violence, brutality, degradation, and various other abnormalities. Society is becoming increasingly hypocritical, the nation is gradually declining, internal problems are intensifying, foreign insults are frequent, the national spirit is weakening, and the country is approaching the brink of collapse. To revive, we must thoroughly cleanse past bad habits and actively renew and strive forward. Therefore, the "New Life" movement is considered by contemporaries to be a way to save the country and strengthen it, which is well-founded. Chaozhou, as an ancient and simple place, has a pure and honest folk style. However, due to prevailing customs, it inevitably follows the trends. This is especially true for fellow villagers living abroad, where extravagance and luxury have become a common practice. This is due to the great influence of the environment. Although a few enlightened individuals have the intention to improve, they are constrained by long-standing habits and intimidated by public opinion, making it difficult to break free. Recognizing this, our association intends to use the power of the group to promote change, organizing the Thrift Society, widely recruiting like-minded individuals, and establishing covenants that are practical and easy to implement, to be observed by all. Through gradual accumulation and sustained effort, we aim to correct deviations, rectify wrongs, and promote renewal, ensuring that acquisition does not harm integrity and giving does not harm generosity, thereby conserving resources, cultivating fine customs, encouraging and assisting each other, and practicing diligently without懈怠. Starting with oneself and influencing others, moving from the shallow to the deep, from the near to the far, and extending to a village and a country, we aim to restore our inherent thrift and become the precursor to national rejuvenation. This is not merely a small contribution to our homeland. This is the reason for the founding.

Postmaster Arrested for Embezzling Public Funds and Fleeing His Post - Telegraph to Hubei Court to Request Extradition 142

Zhang Shisheng, also known as Zhiyuan, from Hubei, aged thirty-nine, formerly served as the second-class postmaster in Huangpi County, Hubei. In August of last year, he was discovered to have embezzled public funds. Zhang abandoned his post and fled without a trace. The provincial post office reported this to the Hubei Provincial High Court, which issued an arrest warrant, and also telegraphed various post offices to be vigilant in their search. After receiving the telegram, the Shanghai Post Office sent a document to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court to issue arrest warrant No. 182. Yesterday, police detectives Yang Yilong and Ren Fengwu of the Chinese detective force of the Public Concession General Police Station, discovered Zhang's hiding place. On the day before yesterday, in the afternoon, they, along with postal inspector Lu Youtong, arrested Zhang at the Wanshun Inn at No. 17, Xinkai River. Yesterday morning, they escorted him to the First Special Court's Criminal Division. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang explained the situation, stating that the post office had telegraphed the Hubei Post Office the night before, requesting the relevant court to send personnel to escort him back. Therefore, this case should be sent to the Hubei Court for investigation and trial. He requested the court to issue a document to the Hubei court to send personnel to escort him back. When questioned, Zhang Shisheng confessed that he had embezzled over five thousand yuan in public funds due to the entanglements with friends. However, the post office had already disposed of his private property, which was sufficient to compensate for the losses. Judge Shide verified the confession and ordered the defendant to be detained. If the Hubei court could not quickly come to extradite him, the court would transfer Zhang to the Shanghai Local Court for trial.

Jian De Bank Case - Both Sides Seek Amicable Resolution 143

A Glimmer of Hope Appears - Court Grants Postponement

It has been more than half a year since the collapse of Jian De Bank. The responsible directors, supervisors, and managers of the bank, including Chai Chuangui, Li Jingwei, Tu Kaizheng, Chen Xifu, Chai Yousheng, Yan Ziyu, Xie Keming, Ou Jiancheng, Ma Suizhi, Zheng Huaigu, etc., have been using the liquidation process as an excuse to intentionally delay various debts. Although over ten creditors, including Wei Haijiang, Wang Ruyao, Hu Qingxiang, Luo Mingji, Xu Bolun, Zhang Yiyuan, Hu Xinpei, Shao Jiaquan, Xin Ji, and Jiu Feng, etc., have filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Local Court against the responsible individuals for fraud and embezzlement, there have been multiple hearings. The defendants either fail to appear under various pretexts, or if they do appear, they shift responsibility to each other. They have refused to hand over crucial account books of the bank, preventing the true cause of the collapse from being determined. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui held another hearing. Few of the ten plaintiffs were present in person, except for Wei Haijiang, who was ill. Even fewer of the defendants appeared in court. Judge Liu, unable to allow the delay to continue, instructed the plaintiffs who were present that the process would now begin with liquidation. However, this type of liquidation would not involve auditing the entire account books of the bank, but only require the defendants to submit relevant account books as quickly as possible based on the claims of each plaintiff. The court would then appoint personnel to conduct the liquidation. The costs of liquidation would be borne by the plaintiffs. He then instructed the lawyer for the defendants to submit the requested account books within two days to one week without delay. He also questioned the lawyer about whether there was a solution for small depositors with detailed debt amounts, such as Hu Qingxiang. The lawyer for the defendants then described the recent consultations with the plaintiffs to reach an amicable resolution, stating that they had repeatedly consulted with Wei Haijiang and others, and that there was a glimmer of hope. This type of resolution was not empty talk and requested a further postponement. The lawyer for the plaintiffs, upon hearing this, immediately stated the plaintiffs' position, believing that if the defendants were truly sincere in reaching a resolution, they should first provide a guarantor. If the funds were not repaid by the agreed-upon date, the guarantor would be responsible. The court instructed the defendants' lawyer to pay attention to the plaintiffs' request for a guarantor. The court then adjourned the hearing and rescheduled it for the afternoon of the 25th of this month.

Continued Hearing in the Shun An Ship Case 144

Further Investigation Still Needed - Ouyang Tai Remains in Custody

Ouyang Tai, the owner of the Shun An steamship of the Shun An Company, reported to the customs at Sandu Ao, Fujian, in September of last year, that he was instructed by manager Chen Youbai to blow up the ship mid-voyage to obtain insurance money. Because he could not bear the sacrifice of all the lives on board, he surrendered and reported the matter. The customs authorities detained Ouyang Tai and transferred him to the Minhou Local Court. The Shanghai Local Court sent police to bring Ouyang Tai back. The Criminal Division has held repeated investigations without resolution, as detailed in previous reports. Yesterday afternoon at 2:30 PM, Criminal Judge Cai Dingcheng held another hearing in the Third Tribunal. For the sake of caution, the judges interrogated the witnesses separately. The first witness, Shi Jiazhuan, manager of Hao Hua Insurance Company, testified that the marine insurance for the goods on the Shun An ship was handled by broker Dong Yulin. If any mishap occurred, the company would work with a public notary to determine the price of the goods. Chen Youbai testified that he did not instigate Ouyang Tai to blow up the ship and that he was being falsely accused. Zheng Akang testified that he had returned to his ancestral home in Fujian on the orders of his brother Zheng Zhongwu (who is the chairman of Shun An Company) to handle his father's funeral. He did not know anything about the ship explosion. Ouyang Tai testified that on September 12th of last year, at about 7 PM, Chen Youbai came to his house and invited him to a private room on the fifth floor of the Yangzi Hotel. He instructed him to sail the ship into the sea and cause it to hit a reef. He also gave him explosives and a water bottle, stating that they would split the profits after the deed was done. He refused, and Chen immediately gave him an insurance policy worth four thousand eight hundred yuan, stating that if he refused, he would be treated in a certain way. At the time, he saw that Chen's words were fierce and his eyes were angry. Fearing immediate rejection might lead to disaster, he vaguely agreed. The next day, the ship left Shanghai and sailed to the middle of the voyage. Zheng Akang, the younger brother of Chairman Zheng Zhongwu, dismantled the telegraph machine and forced him to blow up the ship. He then went to Duwo and reported the matter to the customs. The ship's chief mate, Chen Youxing, and others accompanied him to the customs, which can prove his innocence. If he was indeed an accomplice, why would he surrender and report the matter? He asked the court to investigate. Judge Cai determined that the case still required investigation, ordered Ouyang Tai to be returned to custody, and ordered Chen Youbai and Zheng Akang to remain on bail pending further hearings.

Young Woman Rescued After Jumping into the River 145

Describes Overwhelming Hardships

At approximately 8 PM on the night before last, a young woman dressed in short clothes stood on the Baidu Bridge outside the mouth of the Suzhou Creek. Taking advantage of a moment when no one was paying attention, she threw herself into the river to commit suicide. The current was rapid, but fortunately, a cargo ship was approaching. The crew quickly used a bamboo pole to hook her clothes and rescued her. They handed her over to the water patrol officers Nos. 22 and 32, who took her to the Customs Water Patrol Station. After changing into dry clothes, she stated that her name was Shi Eryuan, aged twenty-six, from Hangzhou. She had been married off at the age of seventeen and worked as a boatwoman. After several years of marriage, her husband discovered that she was romantic and held a belief in absolute love. At the age of twenty-one, her husband sent her to Shanghai and sold her to a brothel (commonly known as a "wild chicken coop") as a prostitute. Her husband received 330 yuan for her body, with the understanding that she would be free after four years. During that period, she suffered greatly and deeply regretted her initial mistake in thinking, which led to her abandonment by her husband. She endured a prostitute's life for four years. Only in June of last year did her term expire. Due to financial difficulties at the beginning of the year, she agreed with the madame to continue as a prostitute for some time until she had the opportunity to redeem herself. However, most of her earnings were deposited with the madame. As of recently, she had accumulated about 360 yuan. On the 5th of this month, she asked the madame to return the money, but instead, she was forcibly kicked out. She is now homeless and has gone without food for three or four days. Rather than starving to death, she would rather die sooner. She was overwhelmed with sorrow. The police officer asked her where the brothel was located, and she said it was at No. 18, Shihe Lane, Er Ma Road. An investigator was sent to investigate and the owner of the brothel claimed that the prostitute was suffering from a mental illness and that her claim about the debt was fabricated. The police officer then summoned the woman's landlord, Chen Wangshi, to the station to persuade her to prevent her from taking the same path again.
