Women's Realm

Mother's Day Reflections 222

— Shun

Today—May 12th—is Mother's Day! What a deeply moving festival this is! A mother's love is above all else! Ms. Ellen Key said: "Mothers who nurture their children are as sacred as the sun!" There is also a Chinese saying, "Even at a hundred years old, a mother still loves her eighty-year-old child!" These all express the supreme greatness of maternal love! Motherly love is not only the source of individual life but also the simplest and most fundamental requirement for human survival! While commemorating Labor Day and National Humiliation Day certainly has social significance, commemorating the great Mother's Day has even greater social and human significance!

However, how should we commemorate it? The Shanghai Chinese Women's Temperance Union has first proposed the following commemoration methods for us.

(1) Those without mothers come on stage to present flowers.

(2) Those far away send letters of greetings; if far away, write articles praising mothers, or donate to charitable organizations to do charitable works that mothers would most like.

(3) Those who disobey their mother's teachings should resolve to correct their mistakes.

(4) Those in this port (Shanghai) use gifts, tours, banquets, etc., to make their mothers happy.

However, these methods, apart from a few people with comfortable lives, are of course impossible for most poor mothers and children to implement. They have no extra money to buy flowers or donate, nor the ability to write articles praising their mothers' virtues, let alone the leisure to accompany their mothers on outings! It seems that the gentlemen of the Women's Temperance Union have not taken into account the vast majority of starving and freezing mothers and children!

We know that there is no mother who does not love her own children, and similarly, there is no child who does not want to be filial to their mother! But what is the reason why there are unfilial children and evil mothers in the world? It is not that they are inherently evil and unfilial, but that society forces them to do evil! Recently, it was reported in various newspapers that in a certain village in Lihuang County, a son ate his mother's corpse due to starvation! This is certainly an extreme example, but generally speaking, in many disaster areas, parents exchanging children to eat is common, and selling children is even more common! Even from today's issue (see "A Note on Japanese Women's Movement"), we can see the huge number of mothers leading their children to commit suicide! And due to financial relationships, parents and children treating each other as enemies is a very common and ordinary phenomenon! Given the above situation, what right do we have to ask them to be filial and loving to each other!

Taking a step back, even if the Temperance Union's commemoration methods can be done, it is still a personal matter and has no social significance! Why? Because each individual commemorates their own mother, and the mother being commemorated may receive temporary comfort, but her suffering as a mother, especially the suffering of motherhood being suppressed under the patriarchal system, still cannot be alleviated. What is the significance of such commemoration? Therefore, if we want to commemorate Mother's Day, we must commemorate it in a social sense! That is, we should commemorate it by relieving the suffering of all mothers and, even more so, by enabling the majority of mothers to obtain lasting happiness!

From this perspective, Mother's Day is closely related to the liberation of our women, especially the issue of maternal protection! Therefore, today we must at least advocate to society: all mothers should have interests and rights in the family, society, and even politically and economically. Only in this way can it be a truly filial Mother's Day commemoration!

A Note on Japanese Women's Movement 223

— Qian

—Promoting the Implementation of the Mother and Child Assistance Act—

The capital of Japan, Tokyo, is like any major city in the world, bustling and prosperous, of course. On the other hand, in this bustling and prosperous place, there are countless people who cut off their own lives, according to the Daily News. But what attracts our attention the most is the large number of "mother-child suicide" incidents where people cut off their own lives because they have no way to make a living.

This fact is most evident in recent years. In 1933, there were thirty-five cases of parent-child suicide, and in 1932, there were thirty-four cases. Among them, fathers led their children in only four cases, while in the remaining thirty-one cases, mothers committed suicide along with their children.

According to a survey by the Central Social Work Association—this is based solely on the articles in the four major newspapers, Tokyo Nichinichi, Osaka Mainichi, Tokyo Asahi, and Osaka Asahi—in the four years from 1929 to 1933, there were a total of 1,008 cases of parent-child suicide. The number of people involved was 2,789, including more than 1,615 children. According to the gender of the "parent" in this statistic, there were 364 fathers and 774 mothers. In fact, the number of mothers was more than double the number of fathers.

Among the reasons, financial difficulties accounted for 324, family discord 116, personal illness 90, mental abnormality 109, unemployment 54, and child illness 21. All of these reasons can be said to stem from economic problems.

It is said that the Japanese Ministry of Home Affairs, from the standpoint of child protection, investigated fatherless poor widows in 1925 and attempted to formulate an assistance act. However, this assistance act has not yet been implemented, and the relief law enacted in 1929 is still in a perfunctory state.

Originally, this relief law was implemented starting in April 1930. Although the Social Bureau of the Ministry of Home Affairs claimed at the time that the total number of people to be rescued would be 150,000 and the total cost would be 8 million yen, in reality, the number of people rescued in 1933 was only:

Children 51,964 people

Pregnant women 130 people

Mothers breastfeeding infants 556 people

Total 52,650 people

Moreover, the amount of this relief was only 20 sen per person per day, although it was later increased to 25 sen, but each household could not exceed one yen per day. How many mothers and children can this relief law actually save? Judging from many examples, not only is it ultimately difficult for people to live on this relief money, but there are also countless cumbersome procedures for receiving the money and people are often unaware of their right to receive it. In addition, there is a sense of contempt on both the giving and receiving sides, so it is difficult to say that this relief has a sufficient effect.

Therefore, recently, women's groups across Japan have organized a League for the Promotion of the Implementation of the Mother and Child Assistance Act, and have made this matter the mainstream of today's women's movement and are petitioning the parliament.

Their argument is that the era when wives were seen as tools for producing family heirs has passed. All children belong to the nation and society, and the nation and society should have the responsibility to protect their lives, and the lives of the mothers who nurture these children should of course be guaranteed.

They also argue that the so-called Mother and Child Assistance Act is different from the relief law. It is the natural responsibility of society to children and to the mothers who raise them. Therefore, the country should enact a corresponding Mother and Child Protection Act in its laws to rescue many mothers and children from malnutrition and the insecurity of death.

Pear Blossoms Stained with Blood 224

— Wu

It is reported that Xu Ming'e, a female student at Zhenguang Middle School in Yantai, was shot and killed after being teased by accompanying policemen while visiting Nanshan to admire pear blossoms. Afterwards, the local student union issued an official statement, saying:

"The entire Zhenguang Girls' Middle School went to Nanshan to admire pear blossoms... Xu Ming'e and seven others wandered to the eastern slope of the mountain stream... Unexpectedly, three security policemen who had been following them for about an hour suddenly approached them and indulged in teasing and playing. One of them, the murderer Kong Fanshu, even took out the box gun he was carrying and aimed it at Xu Ming'e and the others, saying 'Taking a photo.' While hesitating, although the two policemen beside him tried to stop him, Kong declared 'Who are we afraid of now?' As soon as he said this, Xu Ming'e fell to the ground... The investigation found that the occurrence of this tragedy was due to Kong's shallow knowledge, arrogant arrogance, and treating human life as a child's play; and the reason why he acted this way was due to the negligence of duty of the local administrative officials who ruled them..."

Students are still students, with righteousness, enthusiasm, and a sense of right and wrong. From the May Fourth Movement to now, it is the "adults" who have aged, but the students still have their innocent hearts. Originally, killing a few people, shedding some blood, and staining a few flowers red is a really trivial matter. Moreover, the deceased was a woman, and Kong and the policemen had pursued her with bloodshot eyes for an hour, which was already their fault; if it weren't for these students, this matter would have passed without a trace like raindrops. With a badge on his chest and a box gun in his hand, "Who are we afraid of now?" Kong the policeman's bold words are enough to make everyone admire him. When Emperor Shengdu went to Japan, he could have been his attendant and would certainly not have disgraced the country.

Random Thoughts on Reading the Newspaper 225

— Chen Yan

Not long ago, there was news of a Western policeman killing Zhao Liujia, a vegetable vendor. It attracted the attention of people in society, and several groups rose up to support her, demanding punishment of the murderer and compensation for the family. However, there has been no further news since then. Has "punishment of the murderer and compensation" achieved its purpose? One cannot help but wonder!

While a bloody and tragic murder picture is still lingering in our minds, the following record has jumped into my eyes in the newspapers in recent days: "A Dutch member of the Isokuma Circus troupe from England (the police have not announced his name) lured a thirteen-year-old girl who was passing by the circus entrance to come in and watch the show on April 30th. By the afternoon of the third day, a Chinese laborer named Wang Genben helped him rape her. Afterwards, Shan Wang Genben lured her to the Great World for entertainment, where she was spotted by a colleague of her maternal uncle, Zhang Haoyue, who was able to chase and capture them and hand them over to the police. The girl immediately confessed that she, Ge Yin Abe, was the adopted daughter of Yin Shengtao, a current screenwriter and actor at the Tianchan Dance Hall. She then recounted the details of the incident. At the time, the police took the victim to identify the Westerner who raped her and search for evidence, which was quite strict, and instructed Yin Shengtang to go to the police station again the next morning to file a lawsuit with the Dutch consulate and the Second Special District Court. Who knew that when Yin Shengtao went to the police station at three o'clock, the police suddenly changed their attitude and announced in the afternoon that they would not accept the case and would release the witness Wang Genmu. Yin Xintao, feeling that there was no way to seek redress, sent letters to the United Federation of Actors and the Yangzhou Association in Shanghai for assistance." Originally, the law stipulates imprisonment for raping a thirteen-year-old girl, but the consular jurisdiction of imperialists still holds sway in China, and Chinese law is like a Chinese hero who cannot use his martial arts in the concession! Those who suffer the most here are, of course, ordinary people, especially weak women. Chinese women, like Chinese men, are subjected to the political and economic oppression of the imperialists, and also to an additional layer of sexual humiliation. Alas! Imperialism and Chinese women!

Women's groups in Shanghai are numerous, and they should be more courageous than any other group in rising up to support this girl who has been brutally humiliated. This is the proper duty of fighting for national glory.

A Visit to the First Nursery in Beijing 226

— Xian

The sun was setting, it was the time for school to let out, and I walked along the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Dingjiaqiao, past the Central Party Headquarters and Xuanwu Lake, not far north, and arrived at my destination, which was the First Nursery in Beijing, which I had come to visit specifically today, sponsored by the Beijing Women's Cultural Promotion Association.

The nursery is located next to Xuanwu Lake, with beautiful scenery and fresh air. It is a Western-style Chinese building, with a lawn of several feet outside. There are small swings, sandboxes, and other children's play equipment. At the time, it was just the time for school to let out, and some little angels were still left in the playground. Each person wore a bib, some with light green trim and some with purple trim, all provided by the nursery, which were very neat and beautiful. These little angels mostly came from middle-class families, and their parents were educated with new knowledge and worked in various agencies in Beijing. Therefore, they were all unusually strong, clean, lively, and adorable.

After the reporter presented his name card, Ms. Huang Jie, the director of education at the nursery, came out to meet him. Ms. Huang has studied children's education extensively and has been engaged in kindergarten education for nearly 20 years, so her experience can be imagined. This time, she was hired to preside over the nursery's educational affairs and also serve as a childcare instructor. She is purely enthusiastic about public welfare, and no remuneration is discussed. Ms. Huang has six or seven sons and daughters, so she is also experienced in childcare. When she was talking to the reporter, her little daughter was playing in the sand next to her, lively, innocent, and very endearing, truly demonstrating the function of education, which cannot be compared with ordinary children.

The reporter inquired about the nursery's situation, and was introduced by Mr. Huang to Ms. Gong Mulan, the director of the nursery. Ms. Long studied early childhood education in the United States. Ms. Gong then described the origin, development, and current situation of the nursery, and gave me various regulations and forms. Then, she visited the nursery's classrooms, bedrooms, and other interior spaces, guided by Ms. Li Zhishan. Ms. Li is a veteran of the women's movement in Beijing and a key member of the Women's Cultural Promotion Association, and also one of the people in charge of the nursery.

The origin, development, and current situation of the nursery are described below:

(1) Origin—The First Nursery in Beijing is sponsored by the Beijing Women's Promotion Association. The association believes that the most important prerequisite for the modern women's movement is to solve the obstacles to women's work. Married women often have to stop engaging in social undertakings because they are responsible for raising children, which is the biggest obstacle to the women's movement. At the same time, some women must find jobs in society due to economic difficulties and cannot take care of their families. Furthermore, families below the middle class have limited financial resources, and if they do not want to educate their daughters sloppily in the old style, they cannot afford to provide the progressive methods of childcare and the various equipment for the life and education of children of different ages. Even if middle-class families can afford it, it is too uneconomical and unreasonable to waste money building each facility for a small number of children, and besides, not every woman has the talent to raise children well. Therefore, it is impossible for every mother to educate her own children. The ancients exchanged children to teach each other, which shows that China's inherent cultural education also advocates public childcare. Although some people now want to shout the slogan of women returning to the family, modern women only want to move forward. They know that on the one hand, they want to develop their individuality; on the other hand, they want to strengthen the country and build it, and children must have good training, but the two things are contradictory (to be continued).

Lecture on Women's Issues

Section 4: The Right of the First Night 227

— Jun Hui

"The Right of the First Night"—to modern people living in the "civilized" century, it seems like a mysterious and interesting thing in a "One Thousand and One Nights" fairy tale. But this is not a fairy tale, but a fact that did exist in our society more than a thousand years ago. It is not mysterious at all, but a blatant and legal historical fact of the trampling of women.

The so-called Right of the First Night is the superhuman right of feudal lords to sexually exploit serfs. In detail, in the feudal era, when all peasants got married, they had to let the landlord spend the first night with the bride, trampling on her virginity. Therefore, some people say that the lord is the "taster of all marriages."

The Right of the First Night was a legal system in the feudal era and has a long historical basis. According to Bebel, after the collapse of the matriarchal clan, women were exclusively occupied by men, but this violated the rules of the clan. Therefore, in the early days, when women got married, they first practiced sexual openness in the clan before going to marry a specific man. In the feudal era, this custom became the lord's Right of the First Night. This system does not seem to have existed in China, but in Europe, concrete evidence of it has been found in many historical legal documents. In Scotland, King Euvenus III issued a law stipulating that nobles had the right to spend the first night with the brides of all their peasants. This law was amended by King Malcolm in 1075, stipulating that peasants who wanted to redeem their brides' virginity had to pay a certain amount of money. There was also a similar law in France, and in Germany and Switzerland, the Right of the First Night was preserved until the sixteenth century.

With the collapse of the feudal system, the form of the Right of the First Night also changed. That is, peasants who wanted to get married only had to take out a considerable material equivalent to redeem their wives' virginity. In other words, material exploitation replaced sexual exploitation. Regarding this, there is the following passage in Bebel's "Woman and Socialism":

"When serfs and laborers got married, they had to entertain their master and his wife. Thus, the master participated in the wedding ceremony with a cart full of dried salaries. At the same time, the bride and groom presented a quarter of a roasted pig to the master. After the wedding ceremony, the groom had to give his wife's Right of the First Night to the master. If he was unwilling, he had to take out six shillings and four pence to redeem his wife's Right of the First Night."

Feudal lords interfered in the family life and marriage relations of peasants at any time and at will. Lords full of lust were not limited to the Right of the First Night; even in peacetime, they often forced the wives and daughters of peasants to satisfy their animal desires. Leo Sydrowitz, in his "History of Common Customs," repeatedly proved the historical fact that feudal lords arbitrarily trampled on the wives, daughters, and brides of peasants, saying:

"Ancient slaves had to be prepared to sacrifice their bodies at any time to satisfy the lust of their masters. Similarly, half of the women had to (put themselves) at his disposal in order to satisfy the lust of their masters (i.e., lords)."

From the standpoint of our women, the so-called Right of the First Night is not only the sexual exploitation of serfs by lords, but also the most extreme manifestation of the oppression of women's rights by male power. Even if the lord does not interfere in the family life of peasants, the status of women in peasant families is almost zero. The serf's wife is absolutely subordinate to her husband's slave. Not only do they have no freedom of love in the family, but they also bear the burden of difficult production labor, land cultivation and harvesting, livestock breeding, weaving and washing, and other endless labor. If they are not careful, they will be punished by their parents-in-law. Women in feudal society really lived a life of eighteen levels of hell.

Did the Right of the First Night system exist in China? There is no historical data to examine, so it is unknown. But in general, men still value their wives' Right of the First Night very much. In Guangdong, there is still a custom of "eating roasted pig." In detail, on the second day of the wedding, when the groom proves the bride's virginity (i.e., a disguised Right of the First Night system), the groom's family sends several roasted pigs to the bride's family to show their satisfaction. When this custom is linked to the "quarter of a roasted pig" in the quotation from Bebel above, it can be inferred that this system also existed in China.

This disguised Right of the First Night system exists as a very ordinary thing in modern "civilized" society. Modern men are still very concerned about the issue of whether the bride's hymen is broken. And they regard it as a matter of social morality for women. The news that a certain girls' school in Shandong examined the hymens of female students last year, regardless of whether it is true or not, is closely related to men's demand for women's Right of the First Night. However, the male-centered society does not care about the issue of whether the groom is chaste. Therefore, when we understand the Right of the First Night, we should not simply regard it as a special phenomenon of the feudal era. It is undoubtedly true that a disguised Right of the First Night system is practiced anytime and anywhere before the existing power system is eliminated!

Correction 228

The title of Section 3 of Lecture 5 of this lecture (i.e., last week) "Feudal Family Women and Marriage" was originally "Medieval Christendom and Women," which was a misprint. We hereby correct it.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Amateur Ramblings

How to Learn to Write Theoretical Articles? 230

— An Amateur

If you want to write a theoretical article, you must first read a lot of works on that theory. Because you must have a system of that theory in your mind, and have rich content that constitutes this system, then you can write a perfect article about that theory. Secondly, in addition to working hard to read a lot, you also need to write more. I often see many hardworking young friends who have studied a number of theoretical books diligently. When others talk about the theory they are studying, they also know it very well, and sometimes even feel that others are not talking about it well. But if they are asked to talk about it, they cannot systematically express their opinions. What is the reason for this? That is because they just bury themselves in reading and do not write often, and do not regularly organize what they have learned from their research. Also, it is necessary for you to discuss with others, exchange opinions, and stimulate your feelings during research and writing. Therefore, Ouyang Xiu, who was good at writing articles, said: "There are three 'mores' in practicing writing: that is, more reading, more doing, and more discussion."

After the "three mores" of practicing writing have been achieved, you should pay special attention to the methods of writing:

First, every theoretical work must have one or more central ideas. Therefore, when you write a theoretical article, you must first determine the central idea you want to express, and then explain it in order from various aspects. Otherwise, you will be writing randomly, talking nonsense from here to there, and the result is that your article will not be systematic, will not have a center, and others will not understand it. For example, if you want to write an article on the writing style of a literary writer, then you should first determine such a central idea: the writer's writing style is determined by the ideological content he wants to express in his work, by the spirit of the era in which he lives, and by his personal and social environment; then you should use the principles of correct literary theory that you know to explain this central idea, and list the writing styles of literary writers from ancient and modern times, both Chinese and foreign, to prove the correctness of this central idea.

Second, after the central idea is established, you should plan how to organize this central idea and how to construct your theoretical system. To be more specific, you need to determine from which aspects you will explain your opinion; how many large paragraphs should be divided in your entire article. Let's take the above-mentioned article on the writing style of writers as an example. If you have decided to write this article and want to publish the above-mentioned central idea in this article, then you should condense that this article should be divided into these several large paragraphs: (1) What is "writing style"? (2) The content and form of literature, (3) The writer and society, (4) ... Then write down in order. In the middle of this, you need to collect a lot of practical material to discuss the writing styles of many writers from ancient and modern times, both Chinese and foreign, to show the correctness of your theory. Specifically, when you are writing this article, you must stand on the correct position that you know and discuss why classical writers value rules and pay attention to emotions, and why romantic writers are exactly the opposite; why Dostoevsky is so happy to start from the middle of the story when writing, so likes to arrange tense scenes in his works, and so profoundly describes the psychology of his protagonists; why Turgenev likes to start writing from the end of the story and likes to use the law of memory to unfold the story he describes; why the description of Cao Xueqin's "Dream of the Red Chamber" is so gentle, and how the style of his chapter novels appeared... - Based on these practical studies to enrich the content of your article and prove the correctness of your theory. In this way, your article will have practical content, will not be an empty theory, and will therefore be able to resonate with most readers.

Third, in detail, a theoretical article not only has its entire central idea, but also each of its large paragraphs, each of its small sections, and even each of its sentences has a central idea. An article without an overall central idea is an article with completely confused and contradictory theories; if a large paragraph or a small section does not have a central idea, it is also a partial confusion; similarly, if a sentence does not have a central idea, then the sentence is not coherent and cannot be a sentence. You know, the most important thing in a theoretical article is to explain the reasoning clearly, smoothly, and in an organized manner, but an organized, smooth, and clear article is composed of sentences, sections, and large paragraphs that express the central idea. Therefore, when you write a theoretical article, you must not only determine the entire system and divide the large paragraphs, but also clearly organize the central idea of each large paragraph, each small section, and each sentence in order.

Fourth, words and sentences are the foundation of an article, so sentence construction is very important for writing. The words and sentences of a theoretical article use abstract words to explain objective things, so each word and sentence must be in accordance with objective things; otherwise, it will not be coherent. For example, "The lion is a beast" is consistent with objective things and is coherent; but if you write a sentence in a theoretical article, "The lion is a big, beautiful, lively little girl", then it is an incoherent expression full of contradictions that is not consistent with objective things. At the same time, the composition of a theoretical article is to form sentences by combining words, form sections by combining sentences, form paragraphs by combining sections, form chapters by combining paragraphs, and form the full text, so when writing an article, not only must the sentences be smooth and clear, but also each paragraph and each section must be smooth, clear, and orderly.

Fifth, if you already have the above-mentioned knowledge and skills, you should pay attention to rhetoric. Theoretical articles value clarity, conciseness, and power, and sentence construction and rhetoric should be based on this principle. But you must pay attention not to deliberately be artificial, it must be natural. Some people often deliberately do things unnaturally because they pay too much attention to rhetoric, and the result is that it is worse, even making jokes. I once heard that there was an incompetent scholar who went to Beijing to take the exam, and wrote such a funny letter to his family in Beijing: "...Now I send back a pair of foot wrappings and socks. Wrapping means wrapping the feet, and socks means socks. Not saying foot wrapping socks, but saying wrapping socks is an abbreviation. There is a felt hat in the box, dry it when it is sunny, put it away when it rains, otherwise it will mold, mold will rot, and rot will not be a felt hat! My younger sister has grown up, do not let her go out, I am afraid that Wang Ermazi next door will have bad intentions again; however, the wall is several feet high, so it doesn't matter!" Although this is a humorous article in the form of a letter, it can also be used to illustrate the harm of deliberately being artificial in the rhetoric of writing theoretical articles.

Life

Wounded Farmers 231

— Pingwen

My hometown—Jiading is only thirty kilometers away from Shanghai. That place can be said to be a township near a city, and it is also one of the million villages in China.

When I was young, this place was considered a relatively wealthy place among the surrounding villages, but now, in terms of field prices alone, in the past, there were very few people willing to sell for one or two hundred yuan per mu. By the end of last year, farmers who were bankrupt or needed money to pay off debts sold their fertile land at a low price of fifty yuan per mu, and it would still make people shake their heads!

The farmers' production technology, of course, still remains in the ancient empirical era. In addition to believing in their own hands, they also believe in heaven. In five or six years, famines followed one after another. They suffered from locust plagues, and the pain had not yet recovered. Then there was a major flood, and most of the agricultural products were submerged. The government was waiting for relief, followed by the iron hooves of Japanese imperialists, who broke into this broken village on March 3, 1932. The people were displaced, and spring plowing was therefore abandoned. In the following two years, either the weather was long and dry, and the wheat and barley were scorched, or the grain was cheap and hurt the farmers, which was not enough to cover the cost. The farmers' families in the past few years are simply similar to the situation described by the Taoist Banqiao as "selling new silk in May and threshing new grain in September to cure the sore in front of you and dig out the flesh in your heart."

Last year, a dozen or so enlightened people in the county initiated the organization of a cotton production and sales cooperative. On the one hand, they advocated the planting of 100,000-seed cotton and Jiangyin 100-seed cotton, and on the other hand, they formed their own sales office, no longer relying on merchants who exploited heavy profits. But the effect was rarely seen. As for the adjustment of the farmers' economy, it still mostly depends on the local tyrants and pawnshops. Some borrow bean cake and other fertilizers from the local tyrants at high interest rates. If they are unable to repay at the end of the year, the local tyrants force them to mortgage the land deed, writing

Page 20

an interest rate of 20% to 30%, and compound interest must be calculated. In just a few years, the farmers' fields have all been changed to the household registration of the local tyrants. There are also some farmers who, whenever there is a shortage of food, carry bags and packages and wander under the high counter of the pawnshop. As for the Farmers' Bank, although it has been established for a long time, and its business has shown a trend of progress in recent years, it has little effect on the truly poor farmers, and even has nothing to do with the poor farmers. After January 28th, the only ×× pawnshop and its substitutes in the four villages were all closed. The reason, according to their superficial claim, was that they were affected by January 28th. In fact, it was because the pawnshops were not redeemed, so that the capital of the pawnshop owners became sluggish goods, and the financial turnover was not smooth, so they had to close. Later, although wealthy local gentry continued to take over the business under a changed name, this also shows the poverty of the rural economy in general.

Here I want to talk about the local famous specialty, the native cloth. In the past, whenever farmers were idle, the sound of looms could be heard in rural families. The native cloth produced each year could not only be used for clothing for the whole family, but also had a huge amount of exports each year. In the heyday of the native cloth industry, at five or six o'clock every morning, each cloth shop sent people to the market to take orders. At that time, weaving a bolt of cloth could earn two or three hundred wen. Weaving two bolts a day, although only four or five hundred wen of income, was still a small supplement to the farmers' family. However, in recent years, the native cloth industry has plummeted. On the one hand, the sales channels have become narrower, and on the other hand, the selling price has become lower. People who weave cloth see that there is no profit to be made, so they have to imitate the story of cooking cranes and cooking zithers.

Feudal ideology still dominates the entire Jiading. Just talking about the composition of marriage is still entirely a consistent way of buying and selling. There are many cases where people go bankrupt because they marry a wife, scrape around, and cannot repay the debt. Married life often cannot get the slightest happiness. Once a woman marries a husband, she has the idea of ​​following the chicken if she marries a chicken and following the dog if she marries a dog. The power of men dominates everything. Recently, there was a relatively brave woman who remarried a man after her husband died. Unfortunately, the second man also died. In this village shrouded in the old etiquette, she even more bravely automatically married a third man. This can be said to be a novel thing in the old village. It is natural that the woman is looked down upon by everyone. However, the woman's marriage is not due to her own awakening, but is still due to the pressure of life.

On the one hand, the farmers' livelihood cannot be maintained, but on the other hand, in recent years, the dragon boat races, village operas, temple fairs, and other actions that waste money and people have been staged one after another. On the surface, this seems to be a scene of a peaceful world, but who knows that this is dancing on a volcano? Many farmers frown all day long, but the young masters still have no shortage of leisurely elegance. They need sensual pleasure, and they need spiritual stimulation. So they gather a group of well-wishers and launch them to have fun with the farmers.

In this grand event full of elegance and vigor, a few small shops may be able to slightly excite the deserted market like a morphine injection, but what about our farmers? They have to entertain the wealthy relatives who come from afar, especially those snobbish wealthy relatives who come from the city. They usually don't interact with each other, but because of the grand event, the humble door welcomes distinguished guests. The farmers who are eating tomorrow's food today eat chaff and bran themselves, but they have to sincerely entertain the distinguished guests. They pawn their winter clothes out of the back door and bring in big fish and meat from the front door. They face the guests with a bitter smile. What a sad world this is!

Such a township, in China, is only a drop in the ocean, but its disease is precisely the disease of the entire nation, and its demise is precisely the demise of the entire China!

Amateur Coffee Shop

Talking About Fame 232

— Bei

When there were no people in the world, no, when all things were not yet born, the universe was originally just a "formless and nameless" thing, which Lao Tzu called "the beginning of heaven and earth without a name". Later, because of the cleverness of the human brain, all the images of worldly things were given a name, and since then, people have gained a concept of distinction for all worldly things (including people).

To investigate the origin of "name", it was originally just arbitrarily assumed for the sake of facilitating the recognition of things, but once assumed, the world became more eventful because of this.

Since people have given names to all things, and at the same time, there is a distinction between self and others among human beings, the development of "name" has become even more spectacular. First, the so-called "surname" was adopted by people, but because there were still drawbacks of confusion, a "name" was added under the surname, and hawkers and coolies might as well be named Zhang San, Li Si, Amao, Agou, and wealthy merchants were named with blessings, longevity, prosperity, etc. As for literati and elegant scholars, their names must not only strive for elegance such as benevolence, righteousness, loyalty, and sincerity, but also need to take another "style name", and outside the "style name", they take another "pseudonym", and outside the "pseudonym", they take another "alternate pseudonym". The so-called "style name", "pseudonym", and "alternate pseudonym" are all just variations of the name. In ancient times, there were many people who held several "names" in one person.

During the May Fourth Movement, there was a sensational movement to abolish surnames. Mr. Qian Xuantong resolutely advocated "keteing" the "surname" first. In order to show his determination, Mr. Qian took the lead in destroying the "Qian" of Qian Xuantong with one knife, and since then, Xuan Tong of our family has changed to "Doubting Antiquity Xuan Tong". This anecdote should of course be heavily recorded in the history of the evolution of names in the future.

However, people also have various ideas about their own names. One is represented by Zhuge Kongming of the Shu Han Dynasty. He said in the "Chu Shi Biao": "I don't want to be known among the princes." The so-called "I don't want to be known among the princes" means that he does not want to make his "name" known among the princes. He probably also understands the philosophy that "people are afraid of being famous and pigs are afraid of being fat", so he only wants to farm in Nanyang and does not want to be involved in the vortex of struggle. The second type is represented by people who are obsessed with fame and fortune. They are willing to have their names recorded in history books and passed down to future generations. Even when they are alive, they often want their names to be arranged in newspapers in large fonts every day. So they work hard and are afraid that their "name" will not come out! In order to get their own "name" out, they do not hesitate to use all kinds of clever methods, roundabout methods, flattery and horse-shooting. It is quite ridiculous to say, but those who are involved in it do not feel ashamed.

The most famous people at present, apart from those in the political arena, are the most famous movie stars, dance stars, actors, athletes, and swimmers. Like Hu Die's empress, the Liang family's sisters, Mei Lanfang's doctor, Zhou Xianyan's iron gate, and Yang Xiuqiong's mermaid, who doesn't know who?

However, fame is the source of all disasters. The laws of nature are obvious and cannot be avoided. Because Empress Hu Die's name was used as a trademark, it has already caused two companies to sue in the past. Now, the name rights of the mermaid Yang Xiuqiong have been infringed and asked attorney Song Yunhui to declare that there is only one family and no branch in the future. The successive brilliance makes us sigh that we dare not force ourselves to look at this famous name.

According to people, Ruan Lingyu's death was because she was afraid of being burdened by her great fame due to marriage disputes, so she committed suicide. Then fame! Fame! It is actually the source of disaster. Fame can be had and cannot be had!

I remember that someone said: "Bodhi is not a tree, a bright mirror is not a stand. Originally there is nothing, where does the dust come from?" I wonder what those who run after fame and fortune will think when they read these words?

Outlying Postal Agency

Beggars in Guangzhou 233

— Anren

To be fair, everything in Guangzhou has been progressing steadily in recent years. For example, tall Western-style buildings, asphalt roads, huge department stores, magnificent restaurants, automobiles, women, and... well, everything in Guangzhou is constantly increasing and changing. If you don't go out for a few days, you'll feel like everything has changed beyond recognition. However, Guangzhou, like other cities, has a social phenomenon that cannot be improved, and this phenomenon is even expanding day by day in Guangzhou, which is the so-called unsightly beggar class.

Some people may say that I am deliberately exaggerating to attract attention when I say that beggars can form a class. However, according to the actual situation in Guangzhou, they are indeed a part of this society. According to investigations, their actual number reaches more than 40,000. If we take the total population of Guangzhou as a ratio, approximately one out of every ten people is a beggar.

The origins of these beggars vary. Some were born into wealthy families, and were accustomed to extravagance and debauchery. When their wealth was exhausted and they had no skills to make a living, they had no choice but to make the street corner their last resort. Some were born into beggar families (?), and naturally had no opportunity to receive education and learn skills to make a living. Therefore, they inherit the family trade and become beggars with ease. In addition to the above two sources, the tide of unemployment has also swept in many beggars.

Considering the total population of Guangzhou, it is indeed very difficult to constantly provide for the livelihood of one out of every ten people. However, these beggars are not like the beggars in Shanghai, who ask people for money on the street all day long, causing people to feel a headache and resentment at the sight of them. They will never ask others to fulfill their obligations for no reason. Therefore, although there are so many beggars in Guangzhou, it is not like in Shanghai, where you can hear the cries of beggars asking for money wherever you go. They have many ways to make a living, which can be roughly divided into two types: mental labor and manual labor. During the day, manual labor involves picking up cigarette butts on the street, and at night, they carry a broken bamboo basket through the alleys, rummaging through trash cans. Scraps of cloth, waste paper, broken glass, and tin cans are all their targets. Those who are young and strong carry sedan chairs and flagpoles for ceremonial shops, doing similar rough work. Mental labor, on the surface, seems to be very leisurely and comfortable, but it is not easy for those who are not good at scheming to handle. They run around on various roads and streets all day long, trying to find out what weddings, funerals, or other celebrations are taking place in people's homes. They investigate clearly and report back to their fellow beggars, and then send someone to make arrangements at the home of the person holding the event. If it is a wedding, they will paste a red paper strip about three inches long and one and a half inches wide on the wall at the entrance, with the words "Huazi Zhong Ji" (Beggars' Collective Record) engraved on the strip. If it is a funeral, they will paste a blue paper strip on the wall outside, below the foot of the wall, so that people will not notice it. If it is a birth announcement, they will simply ask the household for a red envelope or ginger and vinegar, and also paste a red paper strip on the wall at the entrance. This procedure is similar to the government requiring people to register. When their fellow beggars see this kind of strip, they know what is happening in the household. The households treat these beggars according to their own circumstances: some provide them with food and wine for a day, or just one meal. However, at the very least, they must give them a table of leftovers. When they come here to eat, they are as polite as other guests. Moreover, everyone has to stand in a circle at the entrance and say many auspicious words before the leader of the group goes inside to carry the dishes outside, and then they sit on the ground and start to feast.

They all develop their own methods of making a living to the best of their ability, but their actions are restricted by the group. If there is any transgressive behavior or actions that undermine the group, the leaders will investigate and punish them severely, which is unmatched by the general current laws. The highest authority that manages them is the "Huazi Hui" (Beggars' Association), and all the beggars in the city are members of this association. The organization of this association is like that of ordinary social groups, with a chairman, directors, and other positions. To be a chairman, one must have a deep reputation among the beggars and also have considerable power. If something happens to any member, the chairman must find a way to help. Under this association, there are many small groups, and each group also has an experienced beggar as the group leader. All the actions of the members of this group must be under the command of the group leader. The work they go out to do is assigned by the group leader in advance before they carry it out. If they get any extra money outside, they must bring it back and hand it over to the group leader for distribution without hiding anything.

The job of picking up cigarette butts is very easy. Every day, from morning to night, they wander around the streets or at the entrances of department stores and restaurants, or at movie theaters and train stations, because there are many people coming and going in these places, and the production of cigarette butts is also abundant. However, beggars who are generally experienced in picking up cigarette butts do not pay much attention to cigarette butts on the street, because there are many people coming and going on the street, and the cigarette butts that are left over are not necessarily good quality tobacco, and the selling price is also very limited. Their best destinations are dance halls and high-end movie theaters, or the entrances of high-class brothels. People who come here to smoke do not smoke cheap tobacco, and most of them smoke high-end foreign cigarettes. Moreover, the cigarette butts that are left over are long. The value of picking up one of these cigarette butts is simply several times that of those ordinary cigarette butts.

According to the Social Bureau's investigation, there are about 2,200 people living by picking up cigarette butts here, but the actual number is probably even more than that. In the total number of members of the "Huazi Hui" (Beggars' Association), they account for about 20% or more. Their whereabouts, broadly speaking, are only divided into two major areas: Henan and Hebei. Because business in Hebei is sluggish, only one-tenth of the people work there. Because the business area in Henan is larger, it is further divided into four areas: Henanwei, Fuchangyuan, Dajitou, and Longweidao. Each area has a regional leader who supervises the beggars picking up cigarette butts in this area. In addition to monitoring the actions of his subordinates, the leaders of each area usually also engage in the side business of "second-hand cigarettes." The "extra money" earned by the beggars picking up cigarette butts in each area must be shared with the leader of the area. The leader collects these cigarette butts and estimates them, and after deducting what he is entitled to, he buys the rest with his own money as raw materials for "second-hand cigarettes." The so-called "second-hand cigarettes" are made by mixing all the cigarette butts that are picked up, regardless of quality, and re-rolling them into paper cigarettes by hand, selling them in packs of ten or twenty to coolies and rickshaw pullers at the docks for their enjoyment. The price is of course several times cheaper than ordinary cigarettes. Although these regional leaders are also beggars, their living conditions are not worse than those of rickshaw pullers who live by selling their labor. Their daily income is one and a half yuan at most, and three or four cents at least. But the income of beggars picking up cigarette butts is much less. At most, they can only earn two cents a day, and it is not uncommon to even have "no rice to cook." Fortunately, they are very loyal. If someone has no rice to cook, and someone else gets a good haul, they will still share it with him. Therefore, their two meals a day are not a problem. What they consider difficult to solve is the problem of housing. Because Guangzhou does not have as many alleys as Shanghai for them to use as temporary dormitories, and the number of beggars is so large, they often end up with nowhere to go. Although the Guangzhou authorities have now set up labor offices and civilian shelters to accommodate these beggars, because the number of people is too large, they still cannot accommodate them all.

In short, the more this group of beggars living a special life expands, the more it shows the unrest in society, and at the same time, it is a sign of the decline of a nation!

Weekly Literary Society

Explanation of Poetry 235

— Qitian

Poetry is a branch of literature, and its general nature and function are of course the same as those of literature. However, when it comes to poetry, people immediately think of problems such as "rhythm" and "form." The so-called "rhyme is poetry, no rhyme is prose" is the general explanation of poetry by oriental scholars since ancient times. At the same time, even among Western poets and literary scholars, many people's understanding of poetry is completely based on form and rhythm. For example, the poet Allan Poe said that poetry is "the creation of beautiful rhythm"; Professor Grote said that poetry is "the art of accurately expressing thoughts and emotions in rhymed language to create pleasure"; Leigh Hunt paid special attention to the rhythm of poetry, and he often explained poetry in terms of rhythm.

It is true that poetry has rhythm, tone, and even form. Whether it is ancient or modern, Chinese or foreign, poetry is not absolutely unrelated to these. However, this kind of rhythm, tone, and form are not fixed, and there are no differences and changes in ancient and modern times, Chinese and foreign countries. Five-character poems, seven-character poems, and modern new poems each have their internal rhythm, tone, and form, but they are all different. In modern new poems, there are various different forms. The so-called rhythm, tone, and form can only be used as elements of poetry in such a relative sense. But this is not to say that only poetry has these elements, and nothing else does. In fact, announcements and spells have a certain rhythm, tone, and form, and they have those elements, but they cannot be called poetry. Therefore, we should say that poetry has a certain rhythm, tone, and form, but having rhythm, tone, and form is not necessarily poetry. At the same time, if we absolutize rhythm, tone, and form, and say that poetry must have a certain rhythm, tone, and form, for example, saying that poetry must have a certain number of words per line, a certain number of lines per poem, and must have rhymes, and even each line must have a certain number of stressed or unstressed syllables, then we can say that those who have such rhythm, tone, and form can naturally be called poetry, but those who do not have it are not necessarily not poetry.

From this, it can be seen that the so-called rhythm, tone, and form are not the only fundamental meaning of existence of poetry. It is inappropriate to use them to explain poetry or to define poetry.

Poetry, especially modern poetry, seems to have nothing to do with human life on the surface. Therefore, people's explanations of poetry are most likely to lead to mysterious discussions. The formalists of ancient and modern times, Chinese and foreign countries, of course cannot jump out of the circle of rhythm, tone, and form in their explanations of poetry. The theologians who are closely linked to formalism cannot be separated from the labyrinth of "inspiration" and even God in their explanations of poetry. The famous ancient philosopher Plato said: "Poets do not write poetry by art, but by inspiration, and in a state of divine possession. Therefore, those who are good at poetry must lose their sense of smell when they are writing poetry, just like the dance of the Korybantes. Because poetry is light, it has wings, and it is a sacred creature. Only when inspired, when the senses lose their effectiveness, and when reason loses its control, can one write poetry." This is of course the most mysterious statement. However, it is not surprising that this kind of statement originated in ancient society. The most unfortunate thing is that there are still some professors living in the twentieth century who recognize this statement of Plato in ancient times as correct, and publicly say that "there is indeed something incomprehensible about poetry," which is really the most ignorant expression!

In fact, although poetry is farther away from human social life, it cannot exist without human social life. No matter what form of poetry, or even any mysterious view of poetry, is a product of society. Plato's mysterious opinions originated in ancient slave society; the above-mentioned formalist explanations of poetry are also a reflection of the life consciousness of the people who only seek form and do not talk about content.

We know that singing about love can be said to be one of the main expressions of poetry. But the so-called love is not really dominated by the mysterious god of love. It is also a social phenomenon, and therefore even "pure" lyrical poetry is a reflection of human social life. Ikuchi said: "Those who argue that poetry has nothing to do with all social life are also committing serious mistakes in love poetry. We certainly admit that the root of the poems created by the god of love is often the same. People generally praise the beauty of their lovers. However, the method of expression has undergone profound changes with social changes. If you don't believe it, we only need to compare the love of the Middle Ages or the era of Louis XIV with that of the nineteenth century to understand it. Like the wandering poets, like the knights who worship their lovers with mysterious enthusiasm, like the elegant courtiers of the 'great century' who are eager for fame and whose words are extremely ornate, and finally like the passionate men Musset, Baudelaire, or Hana of the previous century, how profound are the differences in their expressions of passion!" Countless examples of the differences in love in different eras and societies can also be found in China. We see that there are great differences between the love poems in the "Book of Songs," the concept of love expressed in "Romance of the West Chamber," and the love situations depicted in "Dream of the Red Chamber" and "Golden Lotus"? Needless to say, the reason for this difference lies in the society that produced them.

From this, it can be seen that even love poetry is a work of art produced by society.

If we go further to examine the origin of poetry, the problem will become clearer. Here we can quote the following passage——

"Poetry begins where human language begins. The natural calls that accompany the efforts of primitive people are the embryos of words, the initial expression; these calls arise from action, and they are precisely some natural and understandable expressions of action. These labor calls become the root of labor songs. Singing is not just a matter of entertainment or relaxation. When people are working together, lyrics can unite the efforts of workers, giving them a kind of harmony, a rule of rhythm and conformity."

This kind of situation can also be found in many folk songs that are popular everywhere now, so there is no need to make more citations.

In short, whether from the essence, composition, or origin, poetry is inseparable from human social life. Poetry can be said to be the highest form of literature. If literature is an artistic reflection of social life by means of the tool of writing, then poetry, as the highest form of literature, expresses social life in its own unique poetic form—rhythm, tone, and form. The essence and function of poetry, novels, and dramas are not fundamentally different. They are all literature. If we want to say that there are differences between them, then these differences only exist in the external form, and do not exist in their essence.

Biography of a Celebrity

The Pure Poet Shelley (5) 236

— Written by Japanese Tsurumi Yusuke, translated by Zhou Leshan and Qi Junfu

Shelley felt the pain to his core after he realized it. He knew his wife’s strong jealousy was caused by his interaction with other women and the misunderstandings it created. He felt nothing but contempt for his wife from the bottom of his heart.

After all sorts of unpleasant incidents occurred between the two, Shelley realized he could no longer change his wife’s mind, and thus fell into the abyss of pain and despair.

Disappointed with his stubborn wife’s attitude, Shelley walked alone down the street, chanting "Ice-like heart, large block of ice," aimlessly wandering the streets of London. His chest was filled with grief, so sad that he could not even shed tears.

At this moment, like the rising sun in his world, Mary Godwin, Godwin's biological daughter, suddenly appeared. Godwin was still traveling in Scotland at this time.

She was a slender, thin girl with hazel eyes and fluffy golden hair. However, hidden within her weak appearance was a dignified and strong soul. This type of woman, possessing feminine grace and the courage of a lioness, was the ideal woman Shelley was seeking. Moreover, she had her father's inherited intellect and possessed the cultivation to discuss philosophy and poetry in a comprehensive manner. Disappointed with his wife's low level of cultivation, Shelley was guided by this bright star, naturally unfolding like facing the spring sunshine.

However, Shelley, who was completely different from ordinary people, did not hold emotions beyond friendship towards Mary. From his youth, he had a peculiar quirk, which was to strive to illuminate the hearts of those he came into contact with with the light within his own heart. Therefore, regardless of whether the other party was male or female, he only knew how to speak of the truth and beauty of life and enlighten that person. He did not notice how the vibrant, brilliant, and beautiful appearance of his beauty evoked gratitude in the hearts of young members of the opposite sex. He was still innocent and carefree. From this point of view, he was also very ignorant of worldly affairs.

Now he discovered that young and beautiful Mary was his like-minded friend, but how could he know that Mary had fallen in love with him at first sight after their initial meeting!

The two intimately held hands and roamed the suburbs.

She accompanied Shelley to the graveside of her own biological mother—Godwin’s former wife—and sat beside the gravestone. Shelley talked about life and spoke of poetry. And he gave her his long poem *Queen Mab*. At that time, he printed 250 copies at his own expense. It was written when he was eighteen years old.

That night, Mary wrote on the title page of the poem after she returned home:

"Perhaps this title page will not be seen by others, so I dare to boldly write what I want to write. My love for the author of this poem is beyond description. ‘Even if I never belong to you one day, I will never belong to anyone else.’ I swear this in my heart."

Shelley's heart, disappointed with his wife, flowed towards Mary day by day like facing the water. Finally, with the simplicity of a young man, he expressed that he had another love and requested a separation from Harriet. Starting from his principles, he thought that the separation of two people who did not love each other was very legitimate, but the rules of society did not allow it, and Harriet, who had not completely lost her love, was very difficult to agree to. However, Shelley, believing in his wife's infidelity, thought it was improper to continue the worldly form of marriage in any case.

He finally took Mary across the sea and eloped to France. Mary's stepsister, Jane, accompanied them.

From that day on, society began to persecute him severely. This persecution haunted him until his death.

Seven

When the three arrived in Paris, they were penniless.

He pawned his watch and chain for 160 francs. He also borrowed 600 yuan from a banker in Paris with a letter of introduction, and the three began their journey to Switzerland.

They wanted to take a post horse carriage, but they did not have enough travel expenses, so he decided to walk. He then came up with a wonderful idea, which was to buy a donkey to carry the luggage, and the three took turns riding. The next morning, he went to the livestock market and bought a very small donkey. This little donkey carried the three of them, heading far away to the Alps.

Guarded by this young man with the grace of a young girl, the two young ladies rode a small donkey on the village roads of France, which were in turmoil after Napoleon's defeat and the dispersal of millions of soldiers. After walking many miles, the donkey could not walk any further, so Shelley and Jane took turns dragging the donkey.

That night, in the village where they stayed, they sold this little donkey and bought another donkey.

The French villages that had been looted by the invading enemy army were short of food. The so-called inns were just a name. The three of them trembled in the unheated inns. Swarms of rats harassed them from time to time. In this way, they continued their journey.

They were not robbed by bandits, nor did they catch a cold, and they quickly found a small town, Brunnen, on the shore of Lake Lucerne in central Switzerland. They rented two rooms in a villa, bought tables and chairs, and wanted to "live here permanently." But the old stove could not be lit no matter what. The cold winter wind of the Alps kept blowing. He said, "Let's go back," and the next day he hurried away from here and returned to London.

When he stepped into the streets of London, he was penniless as usual. Because he did not have money to pay for the carriage, he ran to the bank, only to find that all the previous deposits had been withdrawn by his wife Harriet. He ran to Harriet's house and only managed to get a few pounds to move into a dirty hotel.

Mary's father, Godwin, forbade his two daughters to interact with Shelley. Godwin's political justice said: "If you marry someone you don't love, it is better to live with someone you love." This kind of thinking penetrated the minds of the young Shelley. Therefore, Shelley wrote a letter to Godwin explaining this intention, but the reply said: "That kind of thinking can be implemented in Utopia, but it is impossible in modern society."

Shelley, who was in difficulty, also heard that his creditors were going to ask the court to issue an arrest warrant, and he might be imprisoned at any time. This debt was caused by the loss of Godwin's cultural enterprise. He managed to borrow more than 10,000 yuan to pay his debt. Not only that, Godwin also asked him for money and urged him by letter.

Alarmed by these many things, Shelley wrote to Godwin saying that he had no reason to do so. On the one hand, he urged him to pay, but on the other hand, he did not allow him to meet him. The old philosopher thought, if he allowed a man who had taken his daughter in an improper way to come to his home, and also borrowed money from that man, he was afraid that the world would criticize him for exchanging his daughter for money, so he only replied that he wanted money, and that meeting was impossible.

Shelley sacrificed a lot of money for this old philosopher, but he did not hate this person. He was a person who did not hold feelings of hatred for those who harmed him. (To be continued)

Movie News

Wildcat Hugging a Lamb 239

The warm sun shines warmly on a small village at the foot of the Great Wall. "Old Man Bitter" Wang Guilin, wearing a tattered cotton-padded jacket, is sunbathing by the haystack. In front of the door, the old ewe, chewing dry grass, is tied up, and a pure white, lovely lamb is suckling at its mother's teat.

Afeng Wang Renmei, who had drifted away, transformed from a village girl to a metropolitan modern lady. Following the Sun Song and Dance Troupe, which travels everywhere to sing, she went north, carrying a rattan bag and a bundle, and returned. She felt the boredom of urban life and the fun of rural scenery. She picked up the pure white lamb and gave a naive smile to the sisters-in-law and sisters who surrounded her.

Star Behind the Scenes 240

(1) Zheng Zhengqiu, Xu Xinfu, and Li Pingqian, three directors, and the Gu sisters, Meijun and Lanjun, etc., went to Hangzhou to attend the 4th Annual Meeting of the China Educational Film Association and have now returned to Shanghai.

(2) Xu Xinfu recently compiled a new script called "Emerald Horse," which has been reviewed and approved.

(3) "Boat Woman," directed by Shen Xiling, will soon be filming outdoor scenes at West Lake, after which the entire film can be completed.

Ye Qiuxin Goes to the Battlefield 241

Ye Qiuxin joined the Star Film Company, playing important roles in "National Soul" and "Big Family," which are enough to show off her acting talent. She plays a brave female student in "National Soul" who leaves her gentle family and steps onto the war-torn battlefield. Yesterday, a scene on the battlefield was filmed. A large trench was set up on the Star Outdoor Photography Site. Barbed wire and sandbags showed a serious war atmosphere. Tense photography work was carried out amidst the sound of artillery fire. When this scene was over, Ye Qiuxin was covered in mud, because some trenches had water in them. However, Ye Qiuxin said: "Filming is really enjoyable. In such a tense and stimulating environment, I feel that life is much more fulfilling. I almost suspect that I have really gone to the battlefield!"

Never Heard Since Ancient Times: Son Becomes Grandson 242

Qin Tong, who is good at playing old men, is showing his skills again in "At the Beginning of Man," playing Wei Heling's father. How his acting skills are, although it cannot be predicted, but based on his past achievements in "Feihua Village" and "Escape," he will naturally give us a satisfying performance in "At the Beginning of Man."

Qin Tong plays Wei Heling's father in "At the Beginning of Man," and his son also has a cameo in "At the Beginning of Man," but plays Wei Heling's son. In this way, his son has become his grandson. Son becomes grandson, don't you think this is a strange thing that has never been heard of since ancient times?

The strange things in "At the Beginning of Man" are not only this one, there are many other kinds of strange things.

Hu Jia Sings "Goddess" Song in Tears 243

Qiezi Girl, who is good at singing and dancing, plays a poor girl who fell into the fire pit in "Boat Woman," singing a tragic "Goddess" song in front of the wine and red lights. When this scene was being filmed, the people visiting the site were all moved by her song. The plot of the play is like this: In a brothel room, the beginning is to shoot the scene of those rich young masters insulting prostitutes, mixed with many unpleasant nonsense words. In extreme unbearable circumstances, the prostitute is forced to urge a song. Hu Jia is playing the role of this prostitute. She swallowed a large glass of wine, stood up and sang the "Goddess" song. Gradually, the moving lyrics grabbed Hu Jia's emotions. When she sang to the middle, Hu Jia's tears could not help but pour out of her eyes. At the end, she was lying on the table, sobbing uncontrollably. Such a scene was performed very movingly by Hu Jia! Everyone felt a little sad.
